(Songjiang) Patrol Chief Arrested for Secretly Smoking Opium

Li Yingqiu, the patrol chief of the Shanyang Dispatch Office of the 9th Public Security Sub-Bureau, usually made his authority felt, abused penalties, and recently extorted money from the sales and smoking shops, causing deep resentment among the local people. There is also a team of the Shanyang Security Brigade, Qin Shihani's troops, stationed there. Usually, when patrols met, they exchanged passwords, but the patrol chief often ignored them, causing great damage to their relationship. Unexpectedly, last night (7th), the patrol chief was smoking opium in a private opium den opened by Feng Guihe, and was seen by the patrol team of the security team. Because he was a serving public official who privately smoked opium, which was illegal, he was immediately arrested and taken back to the team headquarters for temporary detention, awaiting the disposition of the Qin detachment leader upon his return to the headquarters. When the matter was heard by the County Public Security Bureau, believing that the truth was still unknown, they sent personnel to Shanyang to conduct an on-the-spot investigation and await verification.

Winter Follows Spring Order: Peach Trees Bloom

The season is severe winter, but the weather is unusually warm, and ice and snow have not yet been seen. In general, old farmers are afraid that the rice stem borers will be discovered next spring, and the human body also feels uncomfortable. When winter follows the order of spring, it is also a rare creation for peach trees in the countryside to bloom.

(Jiading) Robbery and Injury Outside the West Gate

Song Jiting, a farmer in Pengjia Village, Lianxi Autonomous Experimental Township, outside the West Gate, is a man of modest means. At about 1:00 AM on the 8th, there were more than a dozen bandits, speaking in various accents, dressed as workers, holding flashlights and pistols. They first fired a shot as a warning, and then broke in through the side door, searching the rooms of his son and grandson, losing 870 yuan in cash, as well as gold rings, gold bracelets, and clothes, etc. Song himself was hung up, beaten, and scorched, forced to reveal the whereabouts of the hidden gold, and was seriously injured. His son, Baisheng, had his shoulder pierced by a gunshot. His granddaughter-in-law, Li, had her ear injured by the gold ring being pulled off. Afterwards, the West Gate Public Security Dispatch Office was informed. Inspector Wang Cunhou, on the one hand, telegraphed the Fangtai Public Security Dispatch Office to copy from the southwest to the northeast, and on the other hand, together with the local defense corps, copied from the Gaosheng Bridge and Zhaojing in two ways to the south. But the sky was already bright, and the bandits had fled far away.

Winter Weather with Spring-like Conditions Causes Beans and Wheat to Flower

Since the start of winter, the weather has been warm and mild, with drizzling rain, resembling the climate of spring. Rapeseed in the fields is budding and flowering, broad beans are laden with buds, and wheat seedlings are growing tall. Farmers are worried that if severe cold and frost occur, these tender branches and leaves will wither, making a good harvest unlikely.

(Suzhou) Weiting Blanket Production and Sales Cooperative Established

The handmade blanket industry in the Weiting area is the only handicraft industry in this county. During its peak, it was sold throughout the country, with huge sales volumes. The local Farmers Bank, in order to assist rural areas, plans to invest in revitalizing the industry. The Blanket Production and Sales Cooperative was established yesterday (the 8th). There are a total of 500 weaving households and 2,000 weavers in the area. Each household is a member unit, and one cooperative is established per village. A federation will be formed to govern the cooperatives, and a loan disbursement method has been determined to start investment. It is estimated that the first year of operation will have a surplus of 16,000 yuan. In the future, animal husbandry must also be operated to supply the wool needed locally.

High Court Schedules Retrial for Jin Shuren

The case of Jin Shuren, the former chairman of Xinjiang Province, has been sent to the Jiangsu High Court for repeated trials, but has not yet concluded. He is still detained in the capital. It is now learned that the High Court has scheduled a retrial for the 17th of this month at the Jiangning District Court. It is said that the trial is expected to conclude at that time.

Jiangsu High Court to Move to Zhenjiang

The Jiangsu High Court was reorganized from the High Court Procuratorate and has always been located on Daoqian Street in Suzhou. It is now reported that the Ministry of Justice has decided to move the court to Zhenjiang, with an estimated construction cost of 200,000 yuan. The Jiangsu Provincial Government will provide a subsidy of 30,000 yuan. The original Suzhou site is estimated to be sold for 110,000 yuan, leaving a shortfall of 60,000 yuan, which is currently being planned. Meanwhile, the new building for the Zhenjiang No. 5 Prison is being actively constructed to establish a High Court Detention Center after the High Court moves, to house defendants from various places who are sent there to appeal their cases.

(Wuxi) Agreement Reached on Key Points for Labor Conscription for River Dredging

Zhang Fulin, Director of the Construction Bureau of this county, was summoned to the provincial capital the other day to discuss matters related to the third Wuxi labor conscription for river dredging. As a result, the following three points were agreed upon: (1) The water level of the canal measured in Wuxi is still deep, so dredging will be postponed for the time being. However, the section from Wumu to Shitangwan, which borders Wujin, has already silted up and will be dredged by the province. The Wuxi Construction Bureau should still assist with design and other matters. (2) The silting situation of Huangtiangang was already seen during the floods and droughts this year. The Jiangyin County Government will conduct a survey to prepare for dredging. The Xicheng Canal in Wuxi, which connects to Huangtiangang, has a definite connection, and the Wuxi Construction Bureau should conduct a survey and draw a map to determine whether dredging is necessary based on the actual water level. (3) Wuxi's labor relief dredging of the six major rivers, namely Lujiang, Changguangxi, Nanma Port, Lijian River, Beixingtang River, and Hantang River, and the Xizhang section, is approved. However, the originally planned expenses for building dams and draining water, although budgeted and approved, seem to be slightly larger than those of other counties and should be reduced appropriately to ensure uniformity. The requested subsidy of 15,000 yuan from the province is approved.

Annual Fire Statistics

According to statistics from the Firefighting Federation of this county, there were a total of 140 fires in the 23rd year, of which 111 broke through the roof, and 343 houses were burned down, including 162 straw sheds. Fires were extinguished in time in 28 cases. Three households were insured and handled the claims themselves, and four households were affected. The total insured amount was 68,000 yuan. A total of 13 men, women, old people, and children were burned to death, and 5 people were injured. During the fierce fires, 5 people were rescued, and 15 firefighters were injured. The total loss of houses and property is estimated at more than 315,000 yuan.

Total Number of Land Price Declaration Households

The Wuxi Urban Land Price Declaration Office, after closing the declaration on the 15th of last month, immediately began reviewing the submissions. A total of 24,315 declaration forms were received. However, the review revealed two difficulties: (1) The boundaries of farmland were often difficult to fill in. (2) The house numbers and locations of residences were also not filled in according to the format. Certificates cannot be issued after the announcement, and ownership is also difficult to determine. The office has already notified all households to make corrections. Previously, residents such as Cao Quan and others filed an administrative appeal to the Ministry of Interior based on the Land Law. The Ministry of Interior held that the Suzhou province's handling of urban land price declarations was not aimed at collecting land value tax but was a trial run. The procedures were not inappropriate, and they did not conflict with the Land Law. Therefore, in accordance with Article 8 of the Appeal Law, the appeal was rejected.

(Jiangyin) Robbery at Mopundun in Southern Suburbs

Sun Shi'e, a resident of Yujiaqiao, Masi Township, hired a boat to come to the city on the 5th. When the boat was near Mopundun on Wuyun Bridge in the southern suburbs, three bandits suddenly came aboard, claiming to be inspectors. They searched the boat and robbed clothing and bedding, as well as four dou of white rice. Sun Shi'e is a wealthy man from Yujiaqiao. Fortunately, he had already entered the city and did not suffer any losses. The first substation of the local public security bureau was nearby. After hearing the report, they went to investigate and then reported to the bureau for investigation by the county.

(Changzhou) Construction Department Inspects Long-Distance Buses

Because long-distance buses in various counties have not been inspected since they started operating, the Jiangsu Construction Department will conduct a general inspection in the 24th year to ensure safety. Buses that are dilapidated and unfit for operation will be ordered to stop operating to avoid endangering the safety of travelers. Yao Daru has been appointed to be in charge of this matter. The county government has been ordered to inform the automobile companies to repair all vehicles and await inspection and operation. Yesterday (the 5th), the county government followed the department's order and instructed the Zhenyang Automobile Company to repair all vehicles and wait for inspection before operating.

Rewards and Punishments for Land Reporting

Magistrate Ma of Jiangdu County worked hard to urge land reporting. Although a misunderstanding was caused by the military's surveying in the three districts, after the explanation was given and the situation calmed down, he strictly urged the directors of each district to expedite the process. It has now been found that the districts and townships that have not yet completed the task will be rewarded or punished accordingly. The Gongdaoqiao township in the Eighth District was the first to complete the reporting and received a commendation. The Zhenzhong, Wufu, Chongde, Nanhe, Xuejia, Kangshan, and Fengxiang townships in the First District have also completed the task and received a commendation. The Dayi township in the Eighth District, the Jifeng township in the Third District, the Yiling township in the Sixth District, townships 1 and 2, Yonghe Township 1 in Districts 4, 8, 10, and 11, and Wanshou Township 3 have all completed the task, and the district offices are engaged in adjudication. However, the work in the township offices in the Fourth District is abnormally slow. Magistrate Ma believes that the director of the district, Gao Xinpan, has a wait-and-see attitude and has failed to supervise effectively. He was given a major demerit as a warning.

(Zhenjiang) Civil Affairs Department Trains Township Heads from Southern Jiangsu Counties

In Jiangsu Province, the household registration and baojia organization work in the northern Jiangsu counties was started earlier, and the first phase of work has been largely completed. The Civil Affairs Department ordered the establishment of training classes for township heads, with each period limited to three phases for rotating concentrated training. Currently, counties such as Tongshan have been operating for two to three months or more. Because the baojia organization in the southern Jiangsu counties started later, this training work has not yet been carried out. It is reported that it will begin next month, and the Civil Affairs Department will directly send personnel to the southern Jiangsu counties to conduct training. The baojia chiefs are the basic personnel for implementing baojia, and it is also planned to provide them with training at the same time. It is also reported that an order has been issued to each county that once the third phase of baojia work is completed, household registration changes should be carried out. In urban areas and towns where more sound public security agencies have been established, the public security agencies should be responsible for handling the changes, with the assistance of the district, township, and baojia chiefs. In areas where no public security agencies have been established or where they have been established but are not sound, the district, township, and baojia chiefs are responsible for handling the changes.

Prohibition of Tobacco Seedlings in the Xuzhou and Haizhou Areas

The Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department believes that most of the tobacco seedlings in the province are planted in the Xuzhou and Haizhou areas. Although there have been repeated bans, the results have been minimal. In order to completely eradicate the seedlings,

the department has sent investigators Wang Guobin, Shen Deren, and Long Shuying to strictly prohibit planting in various counties of Baohai. If any are found, they will be dealt with by military law.

Tightening of Government Spending in Liyang and Other Counties

Because the southern Jiangsu counties have been affected by drought, the income from land taxes has been greatly reduced. The provincial government ordered each county to reduce spending as appropriate within the original budget. According to reports, Liyang, Zhenjiang, Lishui, Jintan, Yixing, Jiangpu, Liuhe, and more than a dozen other counties have implemented this measure, with a total reduction of more than 200,000 yuan.

(Jiashan) Discharged Soldiers Rob a Moving Boat

The family of Sun Huanzhi in this city hired a boat the other day to move his eldest son to Songjiang. When the boat was sailing to Changsankouzi, it was suddenly met by five bandits wearing blue military uniforms and speaking with a Hakka accent. They held sharp weapons and ordered the boat to stop. They robbed everything on board, and the boatmen were all beaten. The incident has been reported to the authorities for investigation.

(Jiaxing) Leather Goods Store's Books Kept by Chamber of Commerce

The two leather goods stores, Beililanxiang and Beidajie Xiangtai in Jiaxing, are solely owned by Wang Yongsen. However, due to poor business in recent years, the losses have been huge. As the end of the lunar year approaches, various suppliers are coming to Jiaxing to settle accounts. The owner of the store found it difficult to maintain the business and left a letter and fled the other day. The two stores closed the day before yesterday. A total of more than 23,000 yuan is owed to suppliers and depositors, but the inventory of the two stores is only worth more than 3,000 yuan. The current inventory and books have been kept by the county chamber of commerce. A meeting of creditors will be convened in the next few days.

Special Article

Personal Opinions on Revising the Current Trademark Law (Continued) by He Zhuoxian

3. Regarding the Issue of Trademark Use in China

China's industry and commerce are still in their infancy and cannot compete with the European and American countries where capitalism has developed to its peak. Anyone who pays attention to the world economy and the domestic economic situation can understand this situation. Therefore, in addition to protecting trademark exclusive rights, China's trademark law should also take into account the fundamental shortcomings of the national economy and have a spirit of encouraging the nascent industry and commerce. This goes without saying. The current trademark law permits the registration of the actual first user for identical or similar trademarks (see Article 3 of the Trademark Law), and trademarks that have been used in good faith for more than ten years have the right of priority in registration (Article 4 of the same law). However, if the so-called actual first use and use in good faith for ten years are not restricted, I am afraid that the beneficiaries will not necessarily be the backward domestic industrial and commercial circles, but rather the advanced foreign industrialists and businessmen. China's industrial and commercial development is slow, and merchants have only recently paid attention to trademarks for the past three or four years. However, in European and American countries, after the industrial revolution and the high degree of development of capitalism, the progress of industry and commerce is ten times that of China. Their attention to trademarks is at least half a century earlier than China's. Apart from a few old brands, I dare say that there are not many Chinese trademarks that have a long history of use like those of foreign countries. Under these circumstances, if a Chinese trademark accidentally coincides with a foreign trademark, if the use is less than ten years, it will inevitably be completely defeated by the long history of use of the foreign trademark. Furthermore, if a Chinese trademark has already been registered and a foreign merchant applies to register an identical or similar trademark in China, relying on its history of use in a foreign country, it can use the adjudication procedure (see Article 30, Section 1 of the Trademark Law) to revoke the Chinese trademark that has already been registered. I cannot deny that the greatest function of trademark law is to protect trademark exclusive rights, but when we consider the domestic economic situation and are shocked by the cruelty of economic aggression against China by capitalist countries, we always feel that it is unacceptable for foreign merchants to use their long history of trademark use in their home countries to overwhelm Chinese trademarks (this trend should not be allowed to continue). A good law must fulfill its legal mission, such as a trademark law must be able to protect trademark exclusive rights. However, on the other hand, the law of a country must have characteristics that are suitable for the national conditions of the country in order to be considered complete and without regrets. The current trademark law does not restrict the issue of trademark use, which seems to be a regret from the point of view of (suitability to national conditions). In order to remedy

this shortcoming, I propose that the facts of trademark use should be limited to the facts of use within the territory of China. Then, Article 3 and Article 4 of the current trademark law regarding the order of trademark use should be restricted to (within the territory of the Republic of China). If so, the original articles should be changed to (When two or more persons submit separate applications for registration, the registration shall be granted to the actual first user within the territory of the Republic of China; ...) (Article 3) and (Trademarks that have been used in good faith for more than ten years within the territory of the Republic of China, ...) (Article 4).

4. Regarding Other Issues

(A) Article 19, Paragraph 1, Section 1 of the current Trademark Law stipulates that if a merchant changes his registered trademark without authorization or adds a footnote to use it by means of imagery, the Trademark Bureau may, by virtue of its authority or at the request of interested parties, impose a revocation penalty. This article seems to only bind registered trademarks and cannot bind approved but unregistered trademarks. In fact, registered trademarks and approved trademarks have different times; approved trademarks are published in the Trademark Gazette for six months, and only when there are no objections from interested parties, or the objections have been clarified, can they be registered (see Article 27 of the Trademark Law). Judging from the wording of Article 19, Paragraph 1, Section 1, the so-called registered trademark can be interpreted as (a registered trademark). If this is the case, the Trademark Bureau cannot take action against the unauthorized changes or addition of footnotes to approved trademarks to use it by means of imagery. This has to be said that there are loopholes in the current trademark law. To remedy this loophole, I propose adding (The provisions of Section 1 of the preceding paragraph shall apply to approved trademarks) after Section 3 of Paragraph 1 of Article 19.

(B) Regarding the trademarks that have been used in good faith for more than ten years as stipulated in Article 4 of the current Trademark Law, I have already advocated above that the restriction of use in China should be added. However, after careful consideration, even if there is a restriction on use in China, the privilege granted to trademarks that have been used in good faith for more than ten years is still inevitably too lenient. The so-called use in good faith is that the two words in good faith originally have no certain definition and are ultimately too abstract. Because there is no certain definition, it is difficult to make an accurate estimate of good faith and bad faith. If a merchant deliberately imitates a registered trademark of another person and writes a record of more than ten years of use in his account books in advance and applies for registration with the Trademark Bureau, the Trademark Bureau relies on the record of more than ten years of use in his account books. The account books are indeed true, and it is difficult to find out where his bad faith lies, unless an interested party presents strong counter-evidence to clarify that it is not out of good faith. The Trademark Bureau may not necessarily approve the registration of this type of trademark, but this type of merchant who deliberately imitates other people's trademarks can always take advantage of the opportunity to apply for registration of his trademark to sell goods that are actually imitated, and the legal rights of the registered trademark of others will inevitably suffer great losses. For example, if a merchant acts as an agent for the sale of goods of a certain trademark, he can record the trademark name in the account books and omit the word (agent for sale). After ten years, this agent can apply for registration of the trademark according to Article 4 of the Trademark Law. Under this circumstance, although he is actually embezzling the trademark of others, the only evidence for the competent authority to handle this type of trademark registration - commonly known as (Article 4 registration) - is the account books, and the account books clearly have a record of more than ten years of trademark use, which is as seamless as a heavenly garment, and there are no signs of bad faith to be found. As a result, it is difficult to reject its registration. Judging from the above two examples, it can be seen that good faith is an abstract regulation without a definite definition, and it can cause abuses in every respect. Originally, this article was to give a right of priority in registration to those trademarks with a long history of use before the promulgation of the Trademark Law. After the promulgation of the Trademark Law, all trademarks can be applied for registration in accordance with Article 1 of the Trademark Law. If there is indeed a history of use, it is not impossible to obtain exclusive rights in accordance with Article 3 of the Trademark Law. Therefore, I advocate that the article in Article 4 should be prefixed with the words (Before the implementation of this law) so that cunning merchants cannot rely on this law to carry out disguised imitation. (C) There are special articles in the criminal law for handling counterfeit trademarks, and the jurisdiction belongs to courts at all levels. The Trademark Bureau originally has no right to handle them. However, in cases of counterfeit trademarks, the courts, on the one hand, have no experience in handling trademarks, and on the other hand, they have no files to check. Once they accept the case, they cannot judge its authenticity. Therefore, in the 18th year of the Republic of China, the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce asked the Ministry of Justice to issue a circular to courts at all levels that they should consult the Trademark Bureau before adjudicating trademark lawsuits (see Circular No. 812 of the Ministry of Justice). This method is still being implemented. However, in the minds of most merchants, they always believe that the Trademark Bureau is the only authority to handle trademark matters. When their registered trademark is counterfeited, if the other party's trademark has also been submitted for registration, objections can be raised after approval (Article 27 of the Trademark Law), and adjudication can also be requested after registration (Article 30 of the same law). However, if the counterfeit trademark has not been submitted for registration, they will request the Trademark Bureau to identify the authenticity so that they can file a lawsuit with the court. In the past, the Trademark Bureau has only issued a certificate called (Identification Certificate) for this type of request for identification in accordance with the provisions of Article 36, Section 11 of the Implementing Rules of the Trademark Law. In addition to which of the trademarks of the two parties has been submitted for registration, who has not submitted for registration, and whether they are identical or similar, two copies of the trademark patterns of both parties are also attached. This method is originally very common because it can facilitate merchants to file lawsuits with the court and save the court from consulting the Trademark Bureau again. However, under which article of the current Trademark Law is the (Identification Certificate) issued? I cannot find it after searching the current Trademark Law. I strongly advocate this method of issuing (Identification Certificate) because it is indeed needed in fact, but I do not approve of the competent authority doing things that are not based on law. Therefore, I very much hope that this article will be added to the current Trademark Law (When a trademark that has not been submitted for registration is identical or similar to a registered trademark, the interested party may request the Trademark Bureau to identify it).

Conclusion

In summary, I dare not say that I have pointed out all the imperfections in the current trademark law, and I dare not admit that I have drafted a complete and close plan for revising the current trademark law. However, I feel that due to the evolution of the times, the current trademark law does have some shortcomings in completing the two missions of (protecting trademark exclusive rights) and (adapting to China's national conditions). I am a person who firmly advocates revising the current trademark law. Whether my views can be adopted by the legislative authorities is another question. However, if this article can attract considerable attention from the manufacturers and businesses, or if someone comes forward to discuss the various issues of the current trademark law in more detail, this would be my deepest wish.

Local News

Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee Purchases Huge Amount of Silver for Shipment to Shanghai

Total of 20 Million for Market Stabilization

Further Purchases Required if Situation Persists

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, after the establishment of the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee, a huge amount of silver was purchased from Hong Kong and shipped to Shanghai to stabilize the market. The silver is about to arrive in Shanghai. The details are as follows:

(Tight Money Supply) The Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, entrusted by the Ministry of Finance, jointly formed the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee, which was established on October 19 of last year. The address is located inside the Central Bank of China on the Bund. The committee publishes the exchange equalization rate every day. In view of the extremely tight money supply in Shanghai, the foreign exchange rate in the money market once rose to six jiao. Although the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications designated 10 million yuan to be lent to the money and banking industries to stabilize the financial situation, the money supply has eased slightly. Yesterday, the foreign exchange rate dropped to four jiao, but it has not fully retreated.

(Stabilizing Market Prices) Special committee members Xi Demao, Bei Songsun, and Zhang Peishen consulted and decided that in order to stabilize market prices, in accordance with Article 4 of the organizational outline (The committee may entrust the Central Bank of China to buy and sell foreign exchange and bullion in order to stabilize the market according to market needs) and Article 5 (The committee may entrust the Central Bank of China to import and export gold and silver when necessary), it is planned to purchase silver and ship it to Shanghai to stabilize the market.

(Purchasing Silver) Xin Sheng News Agency reporters learned from banking circles yesterday that the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee's purchase of silver and shipment to Shanghai to stabilize the market has become a reality. The committee has entrusted the Central Bank of China to purchase silver from Hong Kong. All procedures are underway. Once successful, the silver will be loaded onto ships and transported to Shanghai, with a total amount of approximately 20 million yuan. It may arrive in Shanghai within the week.

(To Meet Needs) At the same time, the committee may ship silver to Shanghai at any time according to market needs. It has now been decided that after the first batch of approximately 20 million yuan arrives in Shanghai, further purchases of silver will be made and shipped to Shanghai if the market continues to need it. However, the previous rumor that foreign banks such as HSBC and Mercantile Bank would ship silver back from Hong Kong has not yet materialized because the issue of waiving taxes and exchange equalization tax when the silver is exported again in the future has not been resolved.

Cheng Haifeng, Director of the Chinese Branch of the International Labour Organization

Italian Ambassador Visits Embassy Yesterday for Inspection

A copy of the Letter of Credence was sent to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

The establishment of the embassy in Nanjing or Shanghai is yet to be determined.

According to the New Voice News Agency, the first Italian Ambassador to China, Vincenzo Arangio Ruiz, arrived in Shanghai with his family the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning, he visited the embassy office for inspection. He has also begun copying the Letter of Credence to be forwarded to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs before proceeding to Nanjing. The location of the embassy, whether in Nanjing or Shanghai, has not yet been determined. The embassy office in Shanghai will remain in its current state for the time being. Details are as follows:

(Inspection of the Embassy) At approximately 9:00 AM yesterday, Mr. Ruiz, accompanied by his private secretary, Baron Seddio, and Mr. Gabaglio, the aviation attache, along with Italian Minister to China, Mr. Paulucci di Calboli, visited the embassy office at 555 Jing'an Temple Road and the Consulate-General in Shanghai. He introduced the new and old embassy staff. He returned to his residence for rest at noon.

(Copy of the Letter of Credence) The date of the Ambassador's arrival in Nanjing has not yet been determined. According to diplomatic procedures, an incoming ambassador must first submit a copy of the Letter of Credence to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing for review. Then, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs requests an audience date from the Chairman of the National Government. This process is complex and cannot be completed in a day or two. Therefore, the exact date of the Ambassador's arrival in Nanjing is currently unknown. However, according to embassy sources yesterday, the Chinese secretary, Mr. Rossi, has begun copying the Letter of Credence after the Italian Ambassador's arrival. Once completed, it will be sent to the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for forwarding to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing for review.

(Arrival Date in Nanjing) According to sources at the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the date of Ambassador Ruiz's arrival in Nanjing will be decided by Mr. Ruiz after receiving instructions from Nanjing. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will only request an audience date from Chairman Lin Sen after reviewing the copy of the Letter of Credence and then inform Ambassador Ruiz. Ambassador Ruiz will then choose the date of his arrival in Nanjing. However, in any case, he must arrive in Nanjing one or two days before presenting the Letter of Credence. Yesterday, the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had already telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to report his arrival in Shanghai.

(Embassy Location) The location of the embassy, whether in Nanjing or Peiping, has not yet been determined. However, according to a spokesperson for the Italian Embassy, the embassy may not be located in Peiping in the future. The Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs previously instructed the Italian Legation to move to Shanghai due to the inconvenience of having the legation in Peiping. Therefore, the establishment of the embassy will be either in Nanjing or Shanghai. Until the embassy's location is determined, the Shanghai Legation will remain in its current state.

(Minister Paulucci Returns Home) In addition, the former Italian Minister to China, Mr. Paulucci di Calboli, has reportedly been transferred to work within the Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs. He will depart Shanghai on the Italian liner Conte Rosso on the 15th of this month with his secretary, Mr. Visconti. Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng hosted a farewell banquet for Mr. Paulucci a few days ago.

Ministry of Communications Plans to Join International Load Line Convention

A pioneering step towards integrating China's shipping industry internationally

In the past, China did not join the International Load Line Convention because its shipping industry was still in its infancy. In recent years, domestic shipping companies have been striving for development, and their relationship with international shipping vessels is becoming increasingly close. To promote international navigation and safeguard the safety of people and property at sea, the authorities advocate joining the convention. Thirty countries have already joined. The Ministry of Communications has drafted measures and submitted them to the National Government for review. This is a pioneering step in integrating the domestic shipping industry internationally. It is reported that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will implement it in the future.

Adopting scientific methods for managing files

Chamber of Commerce Requests the City Government to Reduce the License Tax on Medicinal Liquor

Used for treatment,

Not comparable to consumables

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the municipal government yesterday stating: This report is submitted to request a factual investigation. On the 7th of this month, the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Industry Association submitted a report stating, "The association had previously received reports from members Yu Liangxin, Zhirentang, and Songshoutang stating that medicinal liquor in Chinese pharmacies is specifically used for treating illnesses and is not comparable to consumables. Requiring the same license fee, ranging from four to two yuan, does not seem to align with the principle of using taxation for regulation. Recently, there has been an increase in the tax rate, and members have suffered greatly from the economic downturn in recent years, with business declining sharply. They are already struggling to survive and cannot afford to bear additional burdens. For example, Yu Liangxin Co. originally paid four yuan per quarter in accordance with Article 3, Paragraph 2 of the Provisional Regulations on Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax, but this fall they were suddenly ordered to pay the Class A tax, doubling the amount. Class A tax should be paid by those who operate stores exclusively selling all kinds of alcohol, but Yu Liangxin is clearly a Chinese pharmacy and has no basis to pay the Class A tax. This has caused confusion for businesses. Zhirentang, Songshoutang, and others have weak capital and a small scope of business. The economy has become increasingly depleted after the war, making it difficult to survive by taking from one area to make up for another. They originally paid two yuan per quarter in tax, which was a reasonable and compassionate assessment of their actual situation, classifying them as Class C. This fall, they were also subject to double taxation, like tired horses being given a heavy load. The future is bleak, and the struggle is increasingly difficult." The association believes that the decline in the Chinese medicine industry is a well-known fact in society and is a natural phenomenon under the shadow of economic recession. However, their energy is depleted, and their ability to bear burdens is extremely weak. On October 22nd, the association submitted a report to the municipal government requesting that the license tax on medicinal liquor be exempted, but no reply has been received to date. Now, the Laolaiyi Chinese Pharmacy on Doushi Street in Nanshi has sent a letter stating that they were fined eight yuan for overdue payment of the license during the requested exemption period and were also required to pay an additional eight yuan for the Class A alcohol license tax. This is consistent with what Yu Liangxin reported, and since the request for exemption was submitted before the municipal government's approval, the situation is different from intentional delays and seems to be excusable. If the Finance Bureau investigates immediately and applies legal regulations, it will be very difficult for merchants. Therefore, a special report is submitted to the General Assembly, requesting that it forward it to the municipal government, which should understand the people's suffering, sympathize with merchants, and exempt Chinese pharmacies from the medicinal liquor license tax to alleviate their difficulties. The fine imposed on Laolaiyi should be refunded, as it is beneficial to the public." According to this, after investigation, Chinese pharmacies specialize in selling medicines, and the various medicinal liquors they sell are also for treatment purposes. This is different from selling liquor in small quantities to consumers. The industry's request for exemption from the medicinal liquor license tax is not unreasonable. Moreover, according to Article 3, Paragraph 2 of the Provisional Regulations on Tobacco and Alcohol Business License Tax, merchants selling alcohol retail and requiring a Class A license are limited to those who operate stores selling all kinds of alcohol. Chinese pharmacies primarily sell medicines, and medicinal liquor is only one of their ancillary products. Now, they are also required to pay tax as Class A retailers, which is difficult for pharmacies to accept. Therefore, a factual report is submitted, requesting that your government review it and instruct the Finance Bureau to reduce or exempt the medicinal liquor license tax for Chinese pharmacies and to refund the fine imposed on Laolaiyi to alleviate merchants' difficulties, as it is beneficial to the public. Respectfully submitted, etc.

The Emergency Relief Donation Committee also received a reply from the Asia-American Weaving Factory stating that the workers' donations are being handled. Since the company's staff and workers are scattered in various factories, the withholding procedure is more complicated. After collecting them at the end of the month, they will be submitted to the Shanghai Bank.

Yesterday, the Shanghai Bank submitted donations collected from workers as of the 5th of this month, totaling $5,755.59, which was submitted to the Emergency Relief Donation Committee for verification.

Selling New Stamp Tax Law Interpretations Under the False Name of the Chamber of Commerce

Contents Are Full of Errors

The Chamber of Commerce Has Requested a Thorough Investigation

The New Sound News Agency reports that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, considering the stamp tax application methods to be extremely complex, previously compiled and printed a small booklet titled "(Answers to Doubts Regarding Stamp Tax)" based on the stamp tax regulations, for the convenience of merchants and the public. This booklet was sold by the Chamber's Commercial Monthly magazine, and those who purchased and read it found it convenient. Unexpectedly, after the new stamp tax law was enacted by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government, an entity calling itself the "Shanghai Commercial Research Institute" published a book titled "Interpretation of the New Stamp Tax Law." The bottom of the book was printed with the name of the representative, Wang Jinyao, as the publisher, and the general distribution location was listed as either the intersection of North Henan Road and Bazilu, or the side of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce on North Suzhou Road. Furthermore, they printed separate lead-typed leaflets with the words "Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce" added next to "Shanghai Commercial Research Institute," and dispatched personnel to peddle the leaflets and books to various businesses in the city. Businesses, unaware of the situation, were often deceived. After the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce learned of this matter, the Commercial Monthly magazine immediately conducted a detailed investigation and discovered that there was no so-called "Shanghai Commercial Research Institute" at either the Bazilu intersection or North Suzhou Road. The "Interpretation of the New Stamp Tax Law" that they printed was also full of errors. This is because this new stamp tax law, although promulgated, has not yet been implemented, and there have already been revisions to the legal text. If businesses affix stamps based on this interpretation, they will inevitably be penalized. The Chamber of Commerce has reported this to the authorities and requested a thorough investigation, and has also announced the facts to prevent merchants and the public from being deceived.

The Salary Increase Issue for Western Crew Members of Taikoo and Other Western Ships Has Been Resolved, and Work Resumed Yesterday

Another Arbitration Committee Has Been Formed to Decide

The Western crew members (captains, chief mates, second mates, third mates, chief engineers, first assistant engineers, second assistant engineers, and third assistant engineers) of the Taikoo Company's four vessels, namely the Foshan, Taishan, Jinshan, and Longshan, as well as the Tianyi Company's Tianyi vessel and the Tongan Company's Dongan and Xi'an vessels, went on strike on December 29th of last year due to their unsuccessful demands for annual salary increases from the companies. Yesterday morning, a reporter from the New Sound News Agency visited the seamen's association of the Seamen's Party, the seamen's union, the steerage workers' union, and other seamen's organizations and learned that the labor and management sides of the crew members had signed a resolution on the previous day to resolve the issue. The salary increase issue for each crew member will be decided by another arbitration committee. After the signing of the agreement, all ships resumed their voyages. Because the dispute was resolved satisfactorily, all crew members resumed work yesterday morning. However, due to the large accumulation of goods between Hong Kong and Guangdong after the strike, loading and unloading are quite busy.

The Suspect Zhang Wentian in the Murder Case of Mr. Shi Liangcai is Transferred to Hangzhou

The Police Department Expresses Agreement to the Hangzhou County's Request for Transfer

Lawyer Zhang Wentian Requests a Speedy Trial

After Mr. Shi Liangcai, the general manager of this newspaper, was shot and assassinated on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, the Zhejiang Provincial Government offered a large reward and issued a wanted notice for the murderers, vowing to bring them to justice. Multiple suspects in the case have been arrested one after another and are currently under close investigation. Zhang Wentian, a resident of Yongyuan Lane on Tianjin Road in this city, originally from Tongzhou, also known as A'er, was found by the Procuratorate of the Hangzhou County Court to be suspected of being involved in the Shi case. They issued a document to the First Special District Court, requesting assistance in the arrest. The Special Court then issued Arrest Warrant No. 5344, which was handed over to the General Police Department. On December 29th of last year, at 11:00 AM, Detective Zhang Xiaolin was dispatched to Yongyuan Lane on Tianjin Road to arrest Zhang and take him to the police department. The next morning, he was escorted to the court for interrogation and detention. This information has already been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the deadline for the continued hearing of this case arrived. The Procuratorate of the Hangzhou Regional Court also sent two bailiffs to present an official document requesting the transfer of the suspect. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang expressed agreement with the transfer. However, Chen Tingrui, Zhang's attorney, stood up and stated that Zhang has been a resident of the lane in Shanghai for more than twenty years and has never left Shanghai. Not only is he completely unacquainted with Shi Liangcai, but he has also never heard of his name and has absolutely no involvement in the matter. Now that the Hangzhou County Procuratorate has dispatched personnel to escort him, there is no objection. A fair judgment will definitely be obtained in the future. However, he requested a speedy conclusion to avoid innocent detention. Furthermore, this case is quite important, and all parties are paying close attention. Since the Hangzhou County authorities have offered a large reward for the arrest of the murderers, it is inevitable that there will be people who are greedy for profit and hope to obtain the huge reward by arbitrarily framing others. This point should be recorded clearly by the clerk for the reference of the Hangzhou County Court. After verifying and reporting to Judge Qian Hongye, the court immediately ordered that Zhang Wentian be allowed to be handed over to the personnel from the Hangzhou County Court Procuratorate to be taken back for investigation and interrogation.

Flights of China National Aviation Corporation Delayed Yesterday Due to Heavy Fog Along the Coast

According to the Kwok Man News Agency, the weather was overcast yesterday, and heavy fog blanketed coastal areas. All flights of the China National Aviation Corporation were suspended yesterday. However, the Shanghai-Hankou route flew from Hankou to Shanghai at 8:00 AM and arrived in Nanjing at 12:35 PM. Later, due to adverse weather conditions on the Nanjing-Shanghai section, it could not come to Shanghai and returned to Hankou from Nanjing at 1:00 PM in the afternoon.

The company's Shanghai-Guangdong route added a Shanghai-Guangdong flight on Tuesdays and a Guangdong-Shanghai flight on Thursdays. The additions were originally scheduled to begin yesterday. Five passengers had already purchased tickets the day before, one destined for Wenzhou, three for Fuzhou, and one for Shantou. However, due to the weather yesterday, the No. 22 Fuzhou Douglas aircraft, piloted by pilot Foen, will fly from Shanghai to Guangdong this morning.

The International Trade Bureau Introduces Raw Antimony and Peanuts

Export Manufacturers Can Contact the Bureau

China's antimony production accounts for almost 80% of the world's total. The antimony from Shuikoushan in Changning County, Hunan Province, is of the purest quality and is an important raw material for manufacturing bullets and type metal. The Philippine Manila Red Star Automatic Machine Company has sent a letter requesting 20,000 pounds of primary antimony per year and inquiring about the CIF Manila delivery price. Export manufacturers who have this mineral for sale are encouraged to send a letter to the Bureau's Guidance Department for introduction. In addition, the peanuts produced in Shandong Province have a very rich oil content and are shipped to European and American countries in large quantities every year for oil extraction, cooking, and the production of artificial butter or as a substitute for olive oil. Recently, the Marseilles Import and Export Company of Ottawa, Canada, sent a letter requesting the purchase of 100-pound packages of peanuts. Export manufacturers are encouraged to contact the company.

The Case of the Datong Correspondence School Accused of Fraudulent Acquisition of Property

Both Sides Opened Debate Yesterday

The Court Ordered Wang Xingnan to Appear

Lu Yaoming, the president of the Datong Trust Bank Correspondence School, was criminally sued by Wang Xingnan and Wang Xingsheng, two brothers who claimed to be correspondence students of the school, through lawyers, for fraudulent acquisition of property. Lu Yaoming denied that the two Wangs were students of the school and also hired a lawyer to file a countersuit against the two Wangs, claiming that they were actually instigated by Xi Yuehan, the founder of the Chengxin Bank Correspondence School, to fabricate facts and falsely accuse him. He requested that the two Wangs be punished for false accusation. The First Special Court has repeatedly held hearings to investigate the situation, as reported in detail in previous issues. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiang Yinghua continued the hearing. Wang Xingnan was still absent, while Wang Xingsheng presented a letter, stating that it was sent by his younger brother Xingnan from Nanjing. The court then interrogated the defendant, Lu Yaoming, who stated that the Datong Correspondence School applied to the Municipal Education Bureau for registration on February 26th and announced its establishment at the same time. Students began registering on March 5th. Although the enrollment advertisement was published on January 14th, it stated that the registration with the Education Bureau had been approved, but the advertisement draft was written by the advertising company on his behalf. However, Wang Xingsheng and Wang Xingnan were definitely not students of Datong. They claimed to have come to the school to register on February 10th, which was not true, as Datong had not yet begun the work of registering students at that time. Their lawsuit was actually instigated by Xi Yuehan, the founder of Chengxin. This point can be investigated with the Education Bureau, and it will be clear. Datong has a total of 152 students. The court, after examining the numbers on the Datong's receipts for tuition fees, found that they did not match the number of students. He then questioned Shen Bingzhong, an employee of the school, about the reasons for the discrepancy. Subsequently, he interrogated Wang Xingsheng, who stated that he went to register on February 10th and paid the tuition fee to Shen Bingzhong, who gave him a receipt. Lu Yaoming gave him mimeographed lectures, which he placed together and have now been lost. Since registering and paying the fee, he only received three books sent by the school on September 25th and one more on October 9th, which he had previously submitted as evidence. He still has a remnant of the book wrapper. In these months, he had sent letters to the school fifteen or sixteen times, urging them about the correspondence courses, but received no reply. His younger brother, Xingnan, is only twenty years old and used to be an apprentice in a pawnshop, but never worked at the Chengxin School. Judge Xiang then instructed him, saying, "Now you are accusing someone of fraudulent acquisition of property, but you have not been able to produce evidence of paying tuition fees, nor do you have proof of enrollment. How will you prove that you are a student of the school? If you insist on accusing Lu of fraudulent acquisition of property, then Lu has also filed a countersuit against you for false accusation. If it is found that your accusation is false, then you must bear the responsibility for false accusation. Therefore, for the sake of settling the matter and pacifying the people, if you withdraw the private prosecution, then Lu's countersuit can also be dropped to avoid mutual litigation and increase ill will. At present, the facts of this case have been investigated and clarified. If you are unwilling to withdraw the private prosecution, then the debate must begin. You should think carefully about it." Upon hearing the instruction, Wang Xingsheng hesitated slightly and then said, "I originally did not want to get involved in litigation, but because Lu not only published a wanted notice for me but also brought many people to my home to cause me trouble, making me unable to sleep peacefully, I had no choice but to resort to litigation. Now, I can only request the court to investigate and handle the matter and order the two sides to begin the debate." Judge Xiang then ordered both parties to debate on the merits of the case, while the countersuit will be investigated separately. He then ordered that the case be reviewed again on the afternoon of January 15th and instructed Wang Xingsheng to notify Wang Xingnan to appear in court next time to await interrogation.

Negotiations for the Ransom of the Three Crew Members Kidnapped from the Jiahe Break Down

Bandits Demand 60,000 Yuan

Families Unable to Pay the Huge Sum

Ransom Representatives Have Left Hong Kong

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiahe vessel was robbed by pirates on November 4th of last year in Shanwei, and three people, namely, business director Shen Qinxiang, cargo clerk Li Xiaobin, and bookkeeper Ge Liangchen, were taken away. Two months have passed since then. After the bandits investigated the situation of the hostages, they specially summoned the families of the hostages to Hong Kong to negotiate the ransom. The bandits agreed to release the hostages immediately after paying for their food expenses. Unexpectedly, after the hostages' representatives arrived in Hong Kong, the bandits' attitude suddenly changed, demanding a huge sum of money, and the negotiations broke down. Yesterday afternoon, it was learned that the ransom matter could not proceed, and the details are as follows:

Negotiating the Ransom The three kidnapped crew members were indeed poor and had no money. They originally had no ability to pay the ransom. Later, after receiving letters from each person from the bandit's lair, they stated that the bandits had sent people to investigate their family situations and knew that they were unable to pay a large sum of money. Now the bandit leader has agreed to release them leniently, only requiring each to pay a certain amount of food expenses before releasing the three. Therefore, each family followed the instructions in the letter and specially sent a representative to Hong Kong to contact the bandit's representative to negotiate the payment of the food expenses for the three people and conveniently lead the three back to Shanghai. On the family side, because of the difficult situation, it was also agreed that even if the food expenses were paid when the representative went to Hong Kong, the maximum amount should not exceed four or five hundred yuan per person.

Demanding a Huge Sum The representatives sent by the families of Shen and Li and others have been in Hong Kong for many days. It is reported that they have contacted the bandit's representative several times. The bandit's attitude is completely inconsistent with the opinions in the letters received by each family. The bandits demanded that the families of the three kidnapped hostages pay a huge ransom before agreeing to release them. Although the family representatives earnestly stated to the bandits that the three families had no property and relied on wages for their livelihoods. Since being kidnapped, the daily lives of each family have been pawned and begged for survival, and they really have no money to pay. They can only pay a small amount of food expenses. After the bandit representative reported to the bandit leader, the final negotiation was that the bandits demanded a ransom of at least 20,000 yuan per person, and the three had to pay 60,000 yuan before they could be released.

Representatives Return to Shanghai Initially, the families had planned to pay a maximum of five or six hundred yuan for food expenses for the three people, but no more than one thousand yuan. However, it was difficult for the three families to raise even this thousand yuan. They originally planned to wait for the representative to go to Hong Kong, and after the negotiations were settled, they would write back to Shanghai, and then find ways to raise the funds. Now, they have received a letter from Hong Kong stating that the bandits are demanding a huge sum of at least 60,000 yuan before they will agree to release them. Upon receiving this information, the three families believed that such a huge sum could not be afforded by the three families. Even one-tenth of it was actually difficult to do. Therefore, they resolutely ordered the people going to Hong Kong to quickly return to Shanghai, abandon the ransom negotiations, and simply let it go, because the three families would never be able to redeem them financially. The representatives going to Hong Kong have now left Hong Kong and returned to Shanghai.

The Lake Society Produces a Film on Formal Dress Movement

Since the Lake Society launched the Formal Dress Movement, it has been able to make a very good impression on the community, thanks to the efforts of the person in charge, Mr. Shen Tianxin. It is reported that in order to widely promote and realize the movement, the society produced a film on the Formal Dress Movement on the 6th of this month at the Star Film Company. It started at 10:00 AM and was completed at 2:00 PM, with a total of seven acts. The famous director Cheng Bugao of the company served as the temporary director. On that day, the men's formal dress group included Chen Aishi, Pan Gongzhan, Shen Tianxin, Ling Songru, Shen Jiesheng, Shen Yanxiang, and members of the Silk Industry Association. The women's formal dress group included Mrs. Chen Yingshi, Mrs. Chen Aishi, Mrs. Pan Gongzhan, and the four daughters of Shen Tianxin, totaling hundreds of people. The film is divided into seven acts: (1) The chairman of the society delivers a speech, stating that formal dress is related to the national system and has been highly valued in the past dynasties. The Republic of China government has long clearly stipulated that the blue robe and black mandarin jacket are the formal dress for men, and the blue cheongsam is the formal dress for women. All formal dress materials must use domestic goods to avoid the outflow of rights and interests, etc. (2) The Ming Dynasty clothing is performed by Mr. and Mrs. Bao Xiaodie, executive members of the society, one with a gauze hat and red robe, and the other with a phoenix crown and xiapei, dressed solemnly and gracefully. Because Mr. Bao is a famous actor, the performance is particularly brilliant. (3) The clothing of the late Qing Dynasty is performed by Mr. and Mrs. Tang Jifu, executive members of the society, with an official hat and robe and a pearl crown and cloak, resembling the rituals of the deceased Qing Dynasty. The bows and retreats are even more lifelike. (4) Modern formal dress is performed by Mr. and Mrs. Chen Aishi, Mr. and Mrs. Pan Gongzhan, and the Shen Tianxin family, acting out a normal meeting ceremony. (5) The entire men's formal dress group performs, led by Chen Aishi and Shen Tianxin, progressing in order. (6) The entire women's formal dress group performs, led by Mrs. Chen Yingshi and Mr. and Mrs. Pan Xiang, proceeding in circles in turn. (7) The mixed performance of the men's and women's groups is divided into two rows, proceeding in turn.

American Ms. Bauer to Lecture on Color Aesthetics Starting Today

Ms. Katherine W. Bauer, an American aesthetics and color expert, will begin a series of art lectures at the American Women's Club today, starting every Wednesday at 5:30 PM. The general topic is "Color," which is divided into the feelings of color in science, aesthetics, and symbolism, the essence of color, comparisons between East and West, the effects of color, the mutual relationship of colors, the blending of colors, the distinction between quiet and noisy, the harmony and disorder of interior colors in homes, churches, and lecture halls, and the psychological reflections of color, the distinction between tranquility and uneasiness, and other programs. Ms. Bauer has previously given three art lectures in Shanghai. Those who have already received the detailed and thorough theory of Ms. Bauer's lectures should not miss this opportunity, and those who have not yet received Ms. Bauer's wonderful arguments should especially go and listen. All those who deeply understand English, regardless of gender, are welcome. There are six lectures in total, and for the sake of popularizing the study of aesthetics and its commercial applications among Chinese ladies and gentlemen, the lecture ticket fee is only ten yuan for all six lectures.

Police Officer Conniving with Bandits and Fleeing, Head of Xinzha Sub-Bureau Suspended

Deputy Inspector General Temporarily Acting as Concurrent Head

Ruan Kaiki Took Office Yesterday Morning

According to the Kwok Man News Agency, Gong Yikui, the head of the Xinzha Sub-Bureau of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was suspended from his post because a police officer under his jurisdiction, Tian Liancheng, colluded with bandits Ma Hongxi and others on New Year's Day this year to commit armed robbery at No. 245 Tanzihwan, Zhabei. The case involved the theft of foreign currency and ornaments from the home of Xu Jintang, the police chief of the Linping Road Police Station in Zhabei, this city. In addition to sending the confession list of the arrested criminals to the Third Section of the General Bureau for handling, the sub-bureau also issued a wanted notice for the fugitive police officer Tian Xiancheng, but he has not yet been apprehended. However, Gong Yikui, considering that during this winter prevention period, not only did a robbery occur, but it also involved a police officer colluding with bandits and fleeing, a major case, specially prepared a document requesting to be punished for dereliction of duty. After receiving the report, Bureau Chief Wen Chaoji requested instructions from Mayor Wu and issued an order yesterday to suspend Gong Yikui, the head of the sub-bureau, from his post pending further instructions. The vacancy was temporarily filled by Ruan Kaiki, the deputy inspector general of the bureau's inspection office. It is reported that after receiving the order, Ruan went to the sub-bureau yesterday morning to take office.

The Yangtze River's Water Level Drops Sharply

Liujiadu is the Shallowest

The water level of the Yangtze River has been receding very rapidly in recent days. The section of the Yangtze River between Wuhu and Jiujiang, specifically the Liujiadu section, has receded to only 4.66 meters of water depth, excluding the bottom level. Larger riverboats with deeper drafts can no longer load much cargo, and even smaller boats must wait for the tide to rise before they can pass through this section, causing riverboats to be delayed. If it recedes further, riverboats will have to reduce the amount of cargo they carry, otherwise, it will be difficult to pass through.

Record of the Meeting of the United Relief Associations

The Shanghai Charitable Organizations United Association convened a meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM in its conference room. Attendees included Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Gu Xinyi, Wang Binyan, Zheng Yuncen (representative of the Bao'an Nursing Home), Ni Rongtai (representative of the Warehouse Trade Public Welfare Association), Feng Yangshan (representative of the Chinese Jisheng Society), Huang Juntang (representative of the Weizhong Shantang), Wang Junsheng (representative of the Pushan Villa), Sun Yishan (representative of the Huhang Charity Association), Luo Xingyou (representative of the Zhabei Charity Group), Wang Zhongfu (representative of the Guangyi Shantang Chinese Women and Children Relief Association), Ye Shouhai (representative of the Xin Puyu Hall), Huang Xingjie (representative of the Shanghai Charity Group), Chen Wenkui (representative of the Shanghai Disabled Persons' Home), Fang Zhijun (representative of the Renji Shantang), Chen Kaifeng (representative of the Renji Infants' Home), and Qu Wenliu (representative of the Xinwei Relief Association). Chairman Wang Yiting first reported that the Zhabei Charity Group sets up a factory on Liuying Road in Zhabei every severe winter to provide congee. The Association has allocated 1,000 yuan from the funds for the Shelter from the Cold Project as a subsidy. It is estimated that the funds for the Shelter from the Cold Project this year will be far from sufficient, so no funds can be allocated yet. According to a letter from the Zhabei Charity Group, the congee factory has been operating since the 1st of this month, and the number of poor people eating congee is increasing daily, reaching 15,000 to 16,000 people, requiring more than 30 piculs of rice. There are still people who cannot get congee and are given copper coins instead. The space in the factory is not enough to accommodate everyone, and the funds are extremely depleted. It is now proposed to stop providing congee and instead give out rice coupons, 5 sheng for large households and 2 sheng for small households, which is estimated to require 1,000 piculs of rice. The congee factory has only raised about 200 piculs of rice, which is far from enough. It is hoped that each charitable organization will donate as much as they can to help the poor, which would be a great merit. Subsequently, the charitable organizations pledged the following amounts: Shanghai Charity Group 200 yuan, Renji Shantang 100 yuan, Chinese Jisheng Society 100 yuan, Ordinary Villa 100 yuan, Xinwei Relief Association 100 yuan, Lianyi Charity Association 100 yuan, Guangyi Shantang 100 yuan, Yimiao Board of Directors 100 yuan, Weizhong Shantang 100 yuan, Warehouse Trade Public Welfare Association 100 yuan. The meeting adjourned after 6:00 PM.

Suspicious Case of Sudden Death of Chen Xinquan

Waiting for Chen Ding's Case to be Resolved and Investigated

Chen Xinquan (also known as Chen Xinfa), a local resident of Yangjing Town, Pudong, 25 years old, worked at the Pinghu Electric Light Factory. He had just returned home on the 23rd of last month. For some unknown reason, he suddenly died suddenly the day before yesterday. The matter is suspicious. The police station in charge learned that the deceased's wife, Ding, had an affair with someone, and that the deceased may have been murdered. Therefore, Chen Ding and the deceased's cousin, Chen Zhangying, were both detained for questioning and handed over to the General Bureau. It is now known that yesterday morning, Lu Qiuqiao, the local security officer of the 24th Bao and 20th Tu, reported the case to the District Court for an autopsy. After receiving the report, the court appointed Prosecutor Zhao Chuannong in the afternoon, accompanied by Coroner Xuan Zhiming, to cross the river to the scene. The autopsy confirmed that Chen Xinquan had died from poisoning. A death certificate was issued, and the family members were instructed to prepare the coffin and await the police station's transfer of Chen Ding and others for thorough investigation.

Zhang Guanghua Accused of Killing His Younger Brother

The Truth of the Chongdefang Blood Case Comes to Light

Zhang Suddenly Recanted His Confession in Court Yesterday

The Police Stated That the Defendant's Confessions Were All Written in His Own Hand

Zhang Guanghua, a 27-year-old man from Henan, and his younger brother, Zhang Guangzhou, an 18-year-old, lived together in the attic room on the third floor of No. 24 Chongdefang, MinGuo Road, outside the Xiaobeimen of the French Concession, in the home of Mrs. Dai Chen, a landlady from Ningbo. Guanghua originally worked at the Navigation Administration Bureau at No. 208, upstairs at the Enterprise Bank on Sichuan Road, but had recently been laid off. Guangzhou was still studying. On the morning of November 23rd of last year, a little after 4:00 AM, Guangzhou was suddenly stabbed in the neck and died. Guanghua also suffered five or six knife wounds to his head and jumped out of the window through the glass canopy, opening the window of the attic room on the second floor. Yan Jinyao, a fellow tenant, pried open the window and door and went downstairs.

(Shouting for help) The landlady's relative, Lin Shengxiang, went out to call the police, who reported to the French police. The police sent Guanghua to the hospital for treatment and transported Guangzhou's body to the coroner's office to request the Special No. 2 Court to send someone to investigate. Since there were no relatives in Shanghai, the body was buried by a charity organization. All of this was reported in the previous newspaper. Since the case was reported, the police have been conducting a thorough investigation but have made no progress. They waited for Zhang Guanghua to recover from his injuries and brought him back to the police station to begin the investigation, which revealed that the deceased was actually killed by Guanghua. According to rumors, the police investigation revealed that the cause of the case was that Guanghua lost his job and ordered his younger brother Guangzhou to return home, but Guangzhou refused, leading to an argument. That night, Guangzhou had the idea of killing his brother. While Guanghua was sleeping soundly,

(He Stabbed Him Viciously with a Knife) His brother's head. Guanghua woke up in his sleep and fought back, killing Guangzhou. The police investigation has concluded. Yesterday, witnesses Dai Chen (the landlady) and fellow tenants Yan Jintao, Shan Bingchang, Zhu Shengxiang, and neighbor Gu Chen were summoned to the court. Zhang Guanghua (whose head injuries had not fully healed and was wearing gauze and white cloth bandages) was brought to the Criminal Division 1 of the Second Special District Court, where Judge Xiong Huiping and Clerk Tao Zongkan presided over the hearing. First, Gu Shouxi, the police lawyer, presented the case and the detailed investigation process by the police, prosecuting him for murder. Zhang Guanghua (whose head injuries had not fully healed and was wearing gauze and white cloth bandages) testified that his younger brother Guangzhou had always

(Studied in Henan) I received a letter from my father saying that he could not afford to support my younger brother's studies, so I wrote to my brother asking him to come to Shanghai and I would teach him myself. He arrived in Shanghai on January 16th of last year. We, as brothers, had a very good relationship and lived in the same room, sleeping on two beds. Sometimes he was not diligent in his studies, and I would hit him on the head once or twice. He was very obedient to me. He usually did not go out unless I took him. My job was terminated on November 22nd, and I was eager to go home. That night, while I was sleeping, I felt someone stabbing me in the head with a knife, and then stabbing my brother. Because the lights were off at night, there was no one else in the room. I suddenly got up, but I couldn't open the door, so I

(Jumped Out of the Window) Knocked on the window of the attic room on the second floor and went in, then opened the door and went downstairs. The back door was open, so I shouted for help and went out, walking past two or three storefronts. A patrolman came and took me to the police station to report. I had five or six knife wounds on my head. [The judge] asked if your injuries were caused by your brother. I answered, I don't know. [The judge] asked, you admitted to killing your brother at the police station. I answered, no. At this point, the court ordered each witness to be summoned to testify, asking their age, place of origin, address, and occupation. After that, each was ordered to provide a written statement and dismissed. First, the landlady Dai Chen was questioned. I sleep with my son in the room behind the parlor. The defendants, the brothers, lived in the attic room on the third floor. Usually they

(Kept the Door Closed) They didn't often greet or call out. I don't know if their brotherly relationship was good or bad. I go out to sell fish every morning at 5:00 AM and return home at noon. I don't ask about their affairs. On the morning of the 23rd, I heard a loud noise on the canopy behind me in my sleep. I woke up, mistaking it for a fire alarm, and was so frightened that my adopted son went out to call the police. I don't know who the murder weapon that was presented was. Yan Jinyao testified: 41 years old, from Haiyan, living in the attic room on the second floor of Chongdefang. We each mind our own business and usually don't call out to each other. I usually don't go to the defendant's room, and I haven't heard them arguing. On the morning of the 23rd, I heard a very loud sound of lead peeling in my sleep, mistaking it for a thief falling down,

(Shouting for Help) And asking me to turn on the light. So I got up and turned on the light. The defendant jumped in through the window, his face covered in blood, standing on the platform. I helped him down. At that time, fellow tenants and neighbors all came to watch. The defendant came down from the platform and opened the door to his room and went downstairs. When the patrolmen and detectives came, I told them what I had seen. I don't know anything else. Shan Bingchang testified: 23 years old, from Shaoxing, recently came to Shanghai from my hometown. I don't know the defendant. On the day of the incident, my older brother Lin Shengxiang and I were sleeping on the mezzanine on the second floor. First, we heard a loud noise, then we heard cries for help. So I got up and went out to call the police. Patrolman No. 644 was called. When we entered the house together, the defendant came down the stairs. The patrolman then

(Took the Defendant Away) To the hospital. Later, a detective came. I accompanied him upstairs. The detective went into the attic room on the third floor and looked around, saying that someone had died and told us not to move or go in. Then I was left in the front room on the third floor. Lin Shengxiang testified: 21 years old, from Ningbo, living by selling fish, sleeping on the mezzanine on the second floor. My testimony is roughly the same as Shan Bingchang's. Postponement of the National Products Movement Promotion and Relief Exhibition

The Official Opening is Set for February 20th

The Shanghai South China National Products Exhibition Association is Making a Joint Sacrifice

The Shanghai South China National Products Exhibition, sponsored by the Shanghai Chinese National Products Manufacturers Association, has been crowded with visitors since its opening. In order to promote the National Products Year for students, promote the effectiveness of national products, and reward the interest of visitors, the association has issued a notice to all manufacturers to prepare 3,000 pieces of daily necessities, starting from today, and implement a joint great sacrifice until they are sold out. The Shanghai National Products Movement Promotion Conference, initiated by the association, was originally scheduled to open on January 15th. However, because the member manufacturers of the association were all in the accounting period at the end of the lunar year and had no time to participate, they requested a postponement. Therefore, it was decided to postpone the official opening to February 20th, so that each member can prepare in a leisurely manner and participate together to support the good cause.

French police detectives Wang Rusong, Zhang Daorong, Liu Jinrong, and Shen Jinshu received a tip the other day that someone had set up a drug trafficking organization on the second floor of No. 258 French Avenue and asked to be arrested together. After hearing the report, Detective Wang and others went to the address for arrest at about 10:00 AM yesterday. As expected, they arrested Zhang Can (32 years old, from Changzhou) and Zhang Lingrong (25 years old) on the spot, confiscating five large packages of morphine (worth about 50,000 yuan), cash and hundreds of yuan, and a female buyer, Yin Asheng (25 years old, from Changzhou). Chen Genfa Commits Suicide Due to Debt

Chen Genfa (35 years old, from Ningbo), who opened the Chen Fuji Tailor Shop at No. 30 Renji Road, Lan Ni Du, Pudong, was addicted to flower gambling and had lost more than 300 taels of gold over the years. As a result, he was heavily in debt and had pawned all the clothing materials entrusted to him by customers. He was unable to make up for it, and customers demanding their clothes were constantly urging him. Seeing this situation, Chen was extremely worried and had the idea of ​​ending his life. The night before last, he suddenly went to the toilet next to Wharf No. 1 of Huatong and hanged himself with his belt. It was not until yesterday morning that someone caught a glimpse of him and reported it to the police on duty, who went to see it and confirmed it. Then, they reported to the police station, and Lu Shunlong, the local security officer of the 24th Bao and 24th Tu, was ordered to report it to the District Court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Zhao and others were commissioned to go to investigate and confirm the death, and it was instructed to prepare the coffin and await further instructions.

Child Injured Leg While Playing with Gun

Yang Jinsheng, a local man, 26 years old, lives at No. 1, Lane 32, Qimei Road, Hongkou, and is currently a member of the volunteer defense force. He has a self-defense pistol. Yang has a cousin named Zhaofu, 12 years old, who lives at No. 17, Lane 41, Qimei Road. Yesterday afternoon at about 5:00 PM, Zhaofu went to Jinsheng's house to play. Accidentally, he pulled out the drawer of the desk used by Jinsheng and saw a pistol inside. At that time, Zhaofu did not know the danger, nor did he know whether there were bullets in it. While he was playing with it, he accidentally touched the trigger, and the bullet came out with a bang. It hit Zhaofu's left leg, and blood flowed like a river. In extreme pain, he fell to the ground. His family members rushed to see what had happened and saw that a disaster had occurred. They rushed him to the hospital for treatment.
