Free Talk

Philistinism

Gorky has a famous work called (The Song of the Falcon), which writes about a falcon flying into the sky with a yearning for freedom and light. It fell down in mid-air, landing exactly where a grass snake was lying. Its chest was pierced and its feathers were stained with blood, but the brave falcon did not regret it at all. He understood the glory of a battle). The grass snake, which was completely satisfied with the damp, warm burrow life, would not understand the falcon's brave behavior. He mocked the falcon's foolishness. Then he thought... (If the falcon wants to go to heaven so much, the life in the sky must be happy.) So he planned to fly into the sky himself to see clearly, forgetting that (anything that is born to crawl on its belly cannot fly). He shot his body into the air and fell on the rocks. The snake, however, thought that he had already flown into the sky and seen the sky. He laughed and said... (So the taste of flying into the sky means you have to fall down.) So he increasingly felt that those birds who were desperately trying to fly into the sky were (ridiculous), their (desires were crazy), their (inappropriateness for real life), and he triumphantly coiled his body on the rocks.

This (smart) snake is really the best specimen of philistinism. He is content with his own (damp, warm) life, and ridicules those who die for freedom and light as (ridiculous) and (crazy); or he has not formally participated in the battle, and declares that he will (leave the trenches) and still return to his own (damp, warm) old nest! These are the actions of philistines. They are born to crawl on their bellies, and you cannot find the spirit of leaping on them. Gorky said that philistinism represents a parasitic class, they are not productive and specialize in consumption. They promote the philosophy of the least resistance to personal growth, and seek a somewhat stable equilibrium between two forces. Envy, greed, vulgar gossip, mutual slander... these are all manifestations of philistinism.

Gorky's own greatness lies in the fact that he is the most thorough opponent of philistinism. The brave vagabonds and homeless people who love freedom in his early works are all existences that are in sharp contrast to the gray philistines, and radiate forever immortal light. All excellent writers almost all hold infinite contempt and hatred for the lukewarm, stingy, despicable, and vulgar of the civic layer. (Hatred of the civic layer is the first step in morality,) even the conservative Flaubert could not help but say this. Gautier once used fantasy costumes and long hair to fight against the vulgarity of the civic class, scolding the civic layer (only bowing down to five-franc gold coins, and having no other ideals than to preserve their own leather jackets). Pushkin was annoyed by the social upper class's vulgarity and wrote the following angry lines...

(Shame on love, throw away thoughts,

But devote yourself to buying and selling,

Kneel before idols,

Hope for gold and locks.)

However, although the writer himself hated the vulgarity of his own class, he could not agree to the severing of the roots of philistinism, and as a result he himself also (conformed to the vulgarity). Gautier goes without saying, even Pushkin later could not help but compromise with the philistines he despised, put the (lyric poem of free will) back into the (golden scabbard), stabbed the heart of philistinism, and would not stop no matter what, in literary history, only Gorky alone.

Even a great man like Goethe could not escape the criticism of being a (narrow-minded philistine). Goethe showed dissatisfaction with the environment, the pursuit of great causes, and the effort to change life in (Faust). But he sometimes became very conservative. He once said to Eckermann...

(Now there is too much talk about aristocratic politics and democratic politics... But this question was very simple when we were young. At that time, we neither looked at property nor cherished its value, so we were democrats. But if we have acquired some property in a long life, then we must make it safe, not only for ourselves, but also for our children, who are going to inherit our property. So in old age we all become aristocrats, no matter what views we held in our youth.)

After reading this passage, we can hardly believe that it came from the mouth of an (arrogant, worldly contemptuous genius). Why is Goethe such a philistine? This can only be found in the fact that he was a well-behaved young master of the Frankfurt City Council and a minister of Weimar himself.

Words of the Lake

— Liu Ming

(1) Daming Lake

Perhaps because it is winter, the impression Daming Lake gave me was not as interesting or as good as I had imagined or seen in books; the entire lake surface has been cut into water ponds like fields by many small dikes, presumably to be used for planting cattails and other plants in spring and summer. The painted boats that go in to visit Lixia Pavilion and other places can only travel along the canal-like waterways. As for the interest in free floating such as (a flat boat can accommodate me) and (let a reed go as it pleases), it is of course impossible to fully enjoy it on the lake here. Moreover, the small dikes that crisscross the lake cannot be used for people to walk on. Those who are not happy to take a painted boat to travel can only look at the lake at the entrance.

There are not many tourists on the lake, and the painted boats and yachts are deserted at the entrance of the lake, letting the snow pile up. Two or three falcons in the sky hover over the lake, spreading their wings and circling for a long time. A few small boats collecting withered reeds slowly sway in the distant water ponds, which can be regarded as puncturing some of the dull silence.

There are historical sites and scenic spots such as Lixia Pavilion, Beiji Pavilion, and Tie Gong Temple in the lake for tourists to visit, but they do not arouse our interest, just like climbing Thousand Buddha Mountain without liking to visit temples. Because we feel that flying springs, waterfalls, mountains, and wilderness, no matter what, are more lovable than the heavily built palaces.

However, looking at Thousand Buddha Mountain from the lake is excellent. You think, when you are tired of traveling in the desolate lake, you suddenly raise your head and see the snow-capped sloping peaks shining in the sky, who wouldn't suddenly feel refreshed? However, this is not a good point of Daming Lake itself.

Perhaps in spring and summer, when the willows sway on the dikes and the lotus flowers bloom in the lake, the scenery is the most beautiful.

(2) Great Light Lake

Traveling to Daming Lake made me even more nostalgic for the Great Light Lake in Yangon. Although there are no weeping willows hanging over the dikes and no lotus flowers blooming in the lake, the green shade that never fades all year round and the clear lake water that can be seen at a glance make people feel happy at all times. The surroundings of the lake are surrounded by asphalt roads shaded by coconut trees, and the east, west, and north sides are inlaid with lush shrub forests. The heart of the lake is also dotted with some gentle slopes like felt grass. Therefore, it is extremely pleasant to sit, lie, or walk on the lake.

Whenever the golden sunset hangs on the waist of the Great Golden Pagoda, Western white-clothed women come in twos and threes to compete on the lake; and European children in red and green also scatter on the slopes, playing various games. Around Saturday afternoons, the municipal government's music team is arranged at the edge of the lake pavilion to play various entertaining songs. But these are not the reasons that make me happy about the Great Light Lake. What I like are the quiet sand roads that sometimes wind around the lake and sometimes enter the forest, which can pleasantly expose my feet, which have been walking in leather shoes all year round, and take a refreshing country walk; or lie on the grass under the forest where few people go, and let the pleasant tree colors and the charming lake light slowly nourish me.

There are no hawkers, no wine shops or tea shops, and no painted boats carrying wine and food like Daming Lake. Everything feels closer to nature, and the spirits of tourists are more fresh and refreshing. Moreover, the crows of tropical countries fly and crow in the forest in the morning and evening, and the lions and tigers in the zoo roar by the lake, which makes it feel like being in a deep mountain forest. This is also a point that makes it difficult for me to forget the Great Light Lake.

Paradise Lost (Continued)

The countryside is desolate, especially at night in winter and spring, when the dogs bark and the crows cry from time to time, which should add to the lonely atmosphere. But the children can dispel this loneliness. If the countryside can be compared to a ink painting, the children's cries do add a touch of vitality.

Naturally, the reason why children play is not to decorate the deserted facade of the village. They have not yet learned to cover up ugliness. They only know how to entertain themselves. They never consider how much good these entertainments give. They just play as they please, not only forgetting to go home late, but also (forgetting themselves). Therefore, there is still a lot of noise in the field until late at night, and they are unwilling to disperse unless adults urge them several times.

Entertainment is also a kind of education. Recently, it has attracted people's attention. I have not estimated how much value the various ways of playing in the countryside mentioned above have, but it is no less inferior to what is stipulated in schools. It is also a fact that it is too simple.

These simple ways of playing may be primitive, barbaric, and unreasonable in the eyes of educators, but there is no way to deal with it for the time being. Although it is just a group of (lawless) wild children, they will certainly not be uncivilized. However, there are too many restrictions on them from society. Even this barbaric way of playing is going to be lost. Isn't it a great pity?

The reason I lost Paradise was because my family still had some money. My father sent me to school. Then he died. I also reached adulthood, so I had to live like ordinary adults, so it was extremely ordinary. If I still ran to the light field of that paradise and joined that small team, even if it was a moonlit night, I am afraid it would cause an unusual reaction. I am no longer a child. However, every winter and spring evening, I can't help but imagine everything that happened in the field when I was a child. No matter how much distance there is in between, I still yearn for Paradise. Sometimes I sit down for a long time, clearly facing the paper wall, but I see a group of children catching, escaping, arguing, and making noise, and even hear whistles. In between, there is the light, floating sadness that cannot be avoided in life; gradually, I am separated from the children!

The year before last, I accidentally returned home because of an accident. The first thing that came to my mind was the paradise on the threshing floor. I had thought of it even when I didn't come. I don't know how many small comedies and tragedies have been staged on that small paradise, but I can't forget it because of the old feelings.

It was a late autumn night, the weather was not very cold, there was a good moon, and even the trees were illuminated like they should only be in fairy tales; I thought there must be a lot of excitement in the field, and I should use it to warm up my old dreams. But when I walked to the road to the threshing floor, I couldn't help but stop. The field was still very flat and clean, and the moonlight was still crystal clear and bright, but I couldn't see a single figure; even the noise and whistles seemed to be swept away by the cold moonlight together. On the street, I couldn't see anything that looked like a person moving. Only a dog hung its head, dragged its tail, and walked slowly, coughing in its mouth. But it was definitely not a fish bone stuck in its throat. I stood for a long time, and it was definitely not to admire the moon, but just stood there for no reason, letting the cool wind blow on my face. Perhaps I was at a loss. But the children who were (uneducated), of course, would not become extinct, so what happened? It couldn't be such a coincidence. But the next day, things became clear. I saw a child in front of the Earth God Temple, about eleven or twelve years old, thin and small, with a withered face, so withered that he looked somewhat old. It was definitely a child. But this child's standing appearance absorbed me. He stood, sticking out his left foot, in a (rest) posture, but his left arm was across his chest, holding his right elbow joint, and his right elbow joint was bent up. A local-made cigarette was clipped between his index and middle fingers. He looked up and stared at the wild, smoking leisurely. Although he didn't pay attention to the surroundings, anyone would be moved, perhaps surprised. He was a hooligan, a sailor looking forward to his homeland, but wasn't he more like an adult?

Violence initially only affected adults, and children were only indirectly affected. Gradually, adults were not enough to fill that greedy mouth. This poisonous net also captured children. They were stripped of their innocence and forced to take on the tasks of adults. They had to bear the sorrows of adults. All happiness was squeezed out. They were originally children who should only be playing, but they had already picked up cigarettes and smoked like adults. No one has mentioned this yet; where is our (genius)!

These words are only about eight or nine years away from when I was a child. It doesn't seem like a long time, but there have been such big changes in eight or nine years. The children have lost even the paradise that was not so good. Now it is almost three years again. How are the children? Who knows?

Life

— Shen Shengshi

Life should be an adventure, not easy, like swinging in a dream; each person climbs to the spire of the tower of life, and the exhausted in the middle fall and are injured.

The coagulation of heart, blood, sweat, and strength, life is pushing a cart; when the energy is like the oil is dry, once the hand is thrown, the wheel can no longer move forward.

The Fly (8)

—By Pirandello, translated by Xi Dichun

It went to rest on Neri's cheek. From his cheek, now slowly, but with two legs, it ran down to his chin, right to the place cut by the razor, and greedily lingered there.

Chai Lu stared intently and attentively at it there, watched it for a long while, and then, with a suppressed distress, asked in a hollow voice...

(Could it be a fly?)

(A fly? Why not?) the doctor replied. Chai Lu said nothing more; he continued to stare at the fly. Neri, as if numbed by the doctor's words, did not wave it away. Chai Lu ignored the doctor, but he was happy in his heart that this remark had so absorbed his cousin's attention, to the point of standing as still as a stone, so that he did not notice the fly's tickling on his chin.

Ah! If only it were this one! Then they would really... get married! His heart was seized by a deep jealousy, a blind, fierce jealousy towards his young and beautiful cousin. For Neri, life was still full of hope, while on the other hand, life was hopeless for him, Chai Lu—

Suddenly, Neri seemed to finally feel himself being stung, raised his hand to chase away the fly, and used his fingers to rub the small cut on his chin. He turned to Chai Lu, saw the strange smile spreading across those terrible lips, and was somewhat flustered. They stared at each other intently for a moment. Then Chai Lu said, almost without intending to...

(Fly—)

Neri couldn't understand and leaned closer to listen.

(What did you say?) (Fly—) he repeated. (Which one? Where?) Neri asked, his heart pounding, while looking at the doctor.

(Right where you scratched yourself. Certainly.) Chai Lu said. Neri showed the cut on his chin to the doctor.

(What got on there? It's so itchy...)

The doctor looked at the cut, frowning; then, as if to take a closer look, he led him outside the stable. Sa Luo followed him.

What happened again? Chai Lu waited, waited for a long time, with a gripping unease in his heart. He heard people talking loudly outside, and suddenly Sa Luo rushed back into the stable, grabbed the mule, and left without even turning his head, crying

(Ah, my poor little Neri! Ah, my poor little Neri!)

So, it's true then? They're just leaving him here like a dog? He tried hard to prop himself up and shouted twice (Sa Luo! Sa Luo!)

Silence. No one outside. He stopped propping himself up and fell back into a lying position; he began to murmur, so as not to hear the silence of the wilderness, which frightened him. Suddenly he thought he was dreaming, suffering from a nightmare in his fever; but, turning back to the wall again, he saw the fly.

It was there.

Sometimes it would extend and retract its tiny sucking organ, and sometimes it would nimbly wash its slender legs, rubbing them together, as if satisfied. (The End)

To Messrs. Xu Ying, An Ke, Lu Xun, Li Qiao, Guan Hua, Shen Du, Zuo Qi, Fan Hai, Yi Shan, Jing Sheng, Tian Ren, Chen Ming, Bai Sheyi An: Please advise of your recent mailing address. Shen Bao Free Talk Editorial Department

Commercial News

Financial Speculation: Silver Prices Expected to Decline

Speculation Margin Increases by Six Yuan Again

Occasional Selling Pressure Quickly Dissipated by Central Bank Intervention

The gold market continued to rise yesterday due to the decline in the silver market and favorable conditions for buyers. Major sellers were still eager to sell. The exchange rate market was normal, even slightly weak, but due to occasional cash injections by the central bank, market sentiment was unusually excited and prone to prosperity. It was observed that early morning foreign dispatches indicated that the silver markets in both the UK and the US had fallen, and the forward silver price in Monterey had also decreased by half a penny to a full penny. The exchange rate also fell. The price of spot gold in London rose by five and a half pence. There were signs that the US government was easing its silver purchasing program, and there were differing opinions within China's financial community regarding monetary policy. However, most bankers and senior advisors to the Minister of Finance agreed with Song Ziwen's proposal to reduce the exchange rate against the US dollar to 25 US cents, or one-quarter. These news items, which were reported in detail in the newspapers, agitated the minds of speculative investors. Pre-market transactions opened and immediately rose to 71.2 yuan. After the opening, the demand from major buyers varied, but was mostly bullish. However, due to credible news, the Central Bank lowered its listed exchange rates by 1.25 for the British pound and 4.375 for the US dollar. The Customs Gold Unit soared by 0.5%. The standard price for speculation margins rose to 1000.2 yuan. The market sentiment became even more excited and ultimately rose. However, as major players took advantage of the high prices to sell, the market gradually declined. The appetite of banks varied. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation announced a decrease of 1.25 for the British pound and 3.75 for the US dollar. There was considerable struggle after the lower rates were announced, but the exchange rate market was normal and gradually hardened. Major players sold again, and for a time, supply exceeded demand, breaking the 70 yuan mark. Buyers took advantage of the low prices to engage in activity, managing to maintain the level. The announcement of the silver equalization tax remained unchanged. At this time, a Reuters dispatch stated that the congressional budget was expected to reduce the silver coinage tax to US$25,000,000, and the Ministry of Finance's expression of silver policy indicated that Shanghai was rumored to be reducing the silver purchasing program. The market remained relatively stable. However, the exchange rate market remained loose, and banks were also releasing funds, leading to a period of selling activity that turned weak. However, there were quite a few people taking advantage of the low prices to buy, and the Central Bank also intervened to inject spot goods, with prices ranging from 962 yuan to 2.5 yuan, and a speculation margin reduction of 8 yuan. The Guang Gang aggressively supplied contracts, and although there was a pullback, the buying sentiment was still strong. By noon, the overall trend was stable, and the afternoon market turned weak. The market broke the 70 yuan mark immediately upon opening, and selling pressure suddenly increased, causing a decline. Banks were still eager to buy, gradually pulling up the prices. The initial report from the Indian silver market indicated a sharp drop of 12 annas, followed by reports that President Roosevelt's speech had triggered selling pressure in the Bombay market, with new short positions being established, leading to a final result of a catastrophic drop of 1 rupee and 6 annas. The market broke through the 70 yuan mark, and buying sentiment suddenly recovered, causing a rise. Although there was some supply, major players were aggressively buying at the lower prices, making it easier to recover after the decline. The domestic market gradually tightened. Rumors spread that the Central Bank had again injected spot goods, with a price of 964 yuan and a speculation margin reduction of 10 yuan. Buyers became even more eager, and speculator Luo increased his bets, triggering another surge. Banks reluctantly released funds at higher prices, causing a slight decline. At this time, major players fought back with their demand for supply, still struggling, but ultimately, due to the large number of sellers, the Indian silver market rebounded by 7 annas for the second time. The market closed lower. The Central Bank reportedly opened approximately 1,000 or more spot positions, generally 8 yuan lower than the speculation margin. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opened at 972.7 yuan, up 6 yuan from the previous close. It then fell to 2.5 yuan. Hengxing Dafa Yong, etc., advanced to 3.8 yuan. Dafa Yong Dadecheng Tongchun sold off, dropping to 2 yuan. The Central Bank announced its listed exchange rates, with the Customs Gold Unit rising 0.5%. Fuchang Yuanmao Yongheng Yuyuan Kangxiang, etc., competed to advance, rising to 5 yuan. Although Fuxing Yong Yongli Hengyu sold off to 3.5 yuan, they rebounded to 4.7 yuan due to Yuanmao Yong Fuxing Yong's advances. Dadecheng Hengxing Tianfeng mutually sold off, dropping to 1.5 yuan. Huabi bought US dollars for February at 33.75. Shunmao Huixiang still advanced to 3.5 yuan. Dadecheng Fuxing Yong sold contracts, dropping to around 2 yuan. Huixiang Yongfeng continued to advance, with some recovery. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation announced its listed exchange rates, with the British pound down 1.25 and the US dollar down 3.75. Market sentiment remained uncertain, and the exchange rate market also hardened. US dollars for March at 56.25 were difficult to sell. Dadecheng Yuan Yi Hengyu Hengxing Yuanchang Yong jointly sold off, dropping to 69.5 yuan. Hengxing Yu Hengchang Yong Zhentai Shenkang Hengyu, etc., bought in at the lower prices, gradually recovering to above 71 yuan. However, due to Zhaofeng Chang Fuchang Dadecheng Shunmao continuing to sell and being mostly bullish, Yuanchang Yong sold contracts again, retreating to within 70 yuan. Hengyu Fuxing Zhengchang, etc., bought in, recovering to above 1 yuan. The announcement of the silver equalization tax remained unchanged. At this time, Reuters dispatches stated that the US Congress was expected to reduce the silver coinage tax by 75% in 1936, and that there were talks of reducing the silver purchasing program, which was quite stable. Yuan Yi Shunmao Yuanchang Yong Fuxing Yong Qianchang Xiang, etc., continued to supply contracts, and the bullish side slightly wavered, dropping to 68.7 yuan. Huabi wanted to buy US dollars for February at 8.75. Fuchang Ding Kang Jia Kang Yuanmao Yong Qianchang Xiang Dadecheng Yuqing Yong Yuan Kangxiang Yukang, etc., entered contracts one after another. There was news that the Central Bank had opened 350 spot positions at a price of 962 yuan, causing a recovery to 72 yuan. Shengda aggressively sold contracts, and Hongkang Yong, etc., also sold, retreating to 1.1 yuan. Zhengchang Yuan Yi came to buy, gradually rising to 2.7 yuan. Yuanmao Yong sold off at the higher prices, dropping to 1.4 yuan. Hengyu, etc., maintained the level, and the afternoon closed at 971.6 yuan. The market remained stable after the close.

The afternoon market opened at 968.7 yuan. Dadecheng Fuxing Yong Zhaofeng Chang, etc., all sold off, dropping to 7.3 yuan. Citibank bought US dollars for March at 75. At this time, Dadecheng bought in from time to time, while Fuxing Yong Hengyu sold, struggling between 1 and 2 yuan. Later, Yuanchang Yong Shunli Qianchang Xiang Yuan Yi, etc., sold, dropping to 0.05 yuan. Dadecheng continued to aggressively buy again, gradually rising. In addition, there were reports that the Central Bank had opened 210 spot positions at a price of 964 yuan. Yuqing Yong Zhentai Dingkang Dadecheng, etc., re-entered, gradually rising to 5.7 yuan. Fuxing Yong Yuan Yi Shunmao sold contracts at the higher prices, dropping to 3.8 yuan. Dingchang Yi Yu Futai Heng continued to aggressively buy, rising to 5 yuan. Qianchang Xiang Changda Fuyu Dadecheng Shenkang Shunmao, etc., sold off one after another. The Indian silver market rebounded by 7 annas, retreating to 2.6 yuan. The market closed at 972.8 yuan. After the close, Dafa Yong Dadecheng Wanxing came to buy, rising to above 3 yuan. Dadecheng Hengyu Qingyong sold off, retreating to 2.5 yuan. It was observed that the highest price of the day was 975.7 yuan, and the lowest price was 967.3 yuan, with a total fluctuation of 8.4 yuan. As a result, the closing price was 6.1 yuan higher than the previous closing price.

The settlement price was listed by the Central Bank's standard speculation margin price as 1000.2 yuan. According to the closing price, it was approximately 27 yuan higher, which was approximately 4 yuan higher than the previous closing price. The registered price for this month was 958 yuan, and for February it was 972 yuan. The morning water supplement was 958 yuan, and the afternoon water supplement was 959 yuan. The price of pure gold was 967 yuan, reduced by 5 yuan. The spot market was even more popular. This was due to the improved environment, which led to increased buying sentiment. Tianjin goods had already been priced at 1 yuan above the speculation margin, and there were few sellers. After the Central Bank released spot goods in the previous session, it continued to open spot positions yesterday, with Tongfeng Heng Fuchang Dafeng Heng Dadecheng, etc., selling more than 1,000 contracts at prices ranging from 962 yuan to 2.5 yuan, generally 8 yuan lower than the speculation margin. It was heard that there were another 210 contracts in the afternoon at a price of 964 yuan, 10 yuan lower than the speculation margin. This was all due to the shorts posting the difference to close out their positions. The contracts for this month have been completely cleared after today's official sheet settlement.

The market transactions were quite active, with varying demands for supply. However, due to the Central Bank's opening of spot margins, demand generally exceeded supply. In summary, Tongfeng Heng Qingfa Yong Hengchang Yong Hengyu Dafa Yong Yiyu Fuchang Huixiang Dingchang Dingkang Futai Heng Fuxing Wanxing Dadecheng, etc., were on the buying side. Indian Silver Selling Pressure Surges, Local Exchange Market Slightly Tightens

▲Near and Far Terms Gradually Converge

According to foreign dispatches yesterday, all London contracts decreased by 1.25, US silver decreased by 0.25, and forward silver prices also fell by 0.5 to 1 point. Spot gold in London rose by 5.5 pence. The British pound against the US dollar decreased by 0.75, the US dollar against the British pound decreased by 1.5 points, the British pound against the French franc fell by 19 points, and the US dollar against the French franc rose by 0.5 points. The exchange market opened in the morning with a near-term selling price of 1 shilling, 4 pence and 8.75 points for the British pound and 34.5 yuan for the US dollar, which was level for the British pound and tighter by 1.875 points for the US dollar compared to the previous close. The Central Bank announced its listed exchange rates, with the British pound decreasing by 1.25 and the US dollar decreasing by 4.375. The Customs Gold Unit rose by 0.5 points, boosting the morale of Chinese merchants. Although the market was slightly tighter after the opening, the process was normal due to the varying appetite of banks. Chinese merchants sold off slightly. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation announced its listed exchange rates, with the British pound decreasing by 1.25 and the US dollar decreasing by 3.75. The market hardened thereafter, but Reuters' dispatch regarding the US potentially reducing the silver coinage tax provided some support. The silver equalization tax announcement remained unchanged, still levying 6.25%. The general trend was set with the British pound calculated at 1 shilling, 5 pence and 6.875 points. After the opening, banks repeatedly sold off, and the process hardened, but the Central Bank's injection of spot goods made the market relatively stable at noon. The afternoon market was still loose, and Chinese merchants sold US dollars, while banks took the opportunity to buy, providing support. Later, President Roosevelt's speech triggered selling pressure in Bombay. The Indian silver market initially plummeted by 1 rupee and 6 annas. The market tightened due to reports that the Central Bank was injecting funds. Banks sold off at higher prices, and the Indian silver market rebounded by 7 annas, slightly stabilizing. The closing near-term selling prices were 1 shilling, 4 pence and 8.4375 points for the British pound and 34.5625 yuan for the US dollar. Compared to the previous close, the British pound tightened by 0.03125 points and the US dollar tightened by 0.125 points. The futures spread has converged. The day's transaction prices are recorded below.

The morning opened with a near-term selling price of 1 shilling, 4 pence and 8.75 points for the British pound. Zhengjin bought 5.625 points for February, Shanghai sold 75 points for January, Great Britain sold half a penny for February, Anda/Mitsui sold 4.375 points for March, Sassoon sold 25 points for June to Anda, and the Central Bank sold spot goods for 93.75 points to Yuli. The afternoon closed with a near-term selling price of 1 shilling, 4 pence and 9.375 points. Call Loan Market Continues to Decline

The silver dollar market has been relatively loose lately, so the market is also becoming more and more calm, significantly different from last week. Yesterday's call loans only reached two-thirds of last week's volume. The morning and afternoon sessions were both at 4 cents, a decrease of 8 points from the previous day. The water added to call loans was more than four-fifths less than last week. The initial market opened at 1.5 cents, later opening at 1.2 cents, a decrease of 6 points from the previous day, indicating that the market is becoming more stable. The trading volume for call loans was over 2.7 million in the morning, with over 400,000 in new transactions. The trading volume was 800,000 in the afternoon, with over 1.2 million in the small general association. The trading volume for silver pawn loans was over 600,000 in redemptions and over 900,000 in new loans. Bank collections and settlements: Foreign banks collected and settled over 2.9 million in bills, over 500,000 in telegraphic transfers, over 4.3 million in various goods and foreign currency pawn loans, over 1.3 million in foreign exchange settlements, and over 800,000 in special foreign currency loans. 400,000 were deposited into warehouses. Chinese banks collected and settled over 3.4 million in bills, over 900,000 in foreign exchange settlements, over 400,000 in foreign currency loans, over 600,000 in customs duties, over 4.6 million in various goods and foreign currency pawn loans, and over 700,000 in special foreign currency loans. 800,000 were withdrawn from warehouses. Japanese banks collected and settled over 2.5 million in bills, over 800,000 in special foreign currency loans, over 900,000 in foreign exchange settlements, and over 3.8 million in various goods and foreign currency pawn loans. 500,000 were deposited into warehouses. Money shops collected and settled over 32 million in silver notes, over 7.4 million in call loans, over 800,000 in banknotes were recovered, over 900,000 in silver dollars were issued, and over 700,000 in secret-marked banknotes were issued. The cash collected and settled, combined with direct and indirect customer routes, amounted to 100,000 in inflows and 300,000 in outflows. The total number of exchanges on the 8th by the local bill exchange office was 8,876,358.7 yuan, including 4,439,052.1 yuan in silver dollars and 4,437,306.6 yuan in silver dollar transfers. The interest rate for interbank call loans was 2 cents per 1,000 yuan per day, and the discount rate for interbank bills was 2.9 cents per 1,000 yuan per day.

Subsidiary Currency Market Shows Slight Increase

The subsidiary currency market, after continuous declines in recent days, finally showed an increase yesterday. Jiangnan small silver dollars were 847 yuan in both the morning and afternoon sessions, a 2 yuan increase from the previous day. The transaction volume was 6,000 jiao in the morning and 2,000 jiao in the afternoon. Guangdong small silver dollars were 759 yuan in the morning and changed to 758.9 yuan in the afternoon, a slight increase of 0.1 yuan from the previous day. The transaction volume was 220,000 jiao in the morning and 90,000 jiao in the afternoon. Copper coins were 306,500 wen, 500 wen better than the previous day. The transaction volume was 35,247 strings and 500 wen, equivalent to 11,500 silver dollars.

Securities Market Approaches End of Lunar Year, Bond Market Quiet and Uninspired

(Very Few New Transactions Except for Futures Spreads and Closing Trades)

Yesterday, the trend of the Chinese Securities Exchange seemed to have gradually entered a period of consolidation. Call loans were only 4 cents, another 8 points lower than before, but market prices were not excited by this, and buyers were not enthusiastic. Major players continued to sell, making it difficult to see a good turnaround quickly. Due to the slack in market sentiment, the market was desolate. There were very few new transactions except for closing trades and futures spreads. Although call loans had eased and market sentiment was not boosted, even if the environment was good, short positions were not covered. There was no strength to rise and no ease to fall, so the future may not avoid a period of consolidation. Yesterday morning, the market opened with a sudden drop in call loans. Retail investors were not weak in entering the market, but trading was not enthusiastic. Sellers were relatively scarce, and market prices rose, continuing to increase by 1-2 cents to about 4 cents compared to the previous day. The tail-end listing was relatively weak. In the second session, numbers 21 and 48 were heavily sold, and market prices were immediately suppressed, and the trend changed from high to low. The atmosphere changed abruptly, and market sentiment became uncertain. After that, there was a consistent decline, with the larger falls being about half a yuan. The gains in the first session were completely lost. There were no rumors in the market, indicating that although silver funds were slightly eased on the surface, major shorts did not cover, and the purchasing power of retail investors was gradually satisfied. There was no reason for market prices to rise. The afternoon situation was even more chaotic, and trading was extremely quiet. Most people were watching. The market opened calmly, with most prices slightly higher by 1-2 cents, and a few slightly higher by 0.05 to 0.1 cents. Closing prices were mostly slightly lower by about 0.1 cents. As the Lunar New Year approached, there seemed to be a contraction. The market price results were mostly slightly lower by 0.05 to 0.1 cents to 0.3 cents, with two or three types slightly higher by 0.05 to 0.1 cents. The total transaction volume was 9,522,000 yuan. US Railroad Stocks Lead the Gains

The New Feng Foreign Firm reported that yesterday (the 7th), the New York stock market was positively influenced by President Roosevelt's budget address. Railroad stocks led the advance. While traders felt uneasy about the unbalanced 1936 budget, this was offset by the President's declaration that there were no plans to impose new taxes. Steel stocks rose due to increased steel production last week. Railroad stocks also rose because it was widely expected that the government would soon provide relief to various routes. The bond market was strong and active, with a very positive reaction to the budget address. Stocks on the small exchange also rose. The total daily turnover was 1.29 million shares. Yarn and Cotton, Japanese Yarn Merchants Swapping Short Positions

Transaction Volume of Marked Yarn Gradually Decreasing

The yarn market is stable, but the situation is unusually scattered. Trading in the market is becoming increasingly quiet because merchants find it difficult to change their habits. The end of the lunar year is approaching, and the scope of business operations is gradually shrinking. Therefore, both buyers and sellers are taking a wait-and-see attitude. Many blackboards are being cleared, and market fluctuations are becoming minimal. However, Japanese merchants have already begun swapping their short positions.

(Golden Rooster Quietly Firm) The opening of the marked yarn market was up, and the market sentiment appeared good. Due to the rise in US cotton, Mr. Wu is still taking delivery this month, which further stabilized people's confidence. However, trading in the market was unusually quiet, and major long and short traders remained inactive. As a result, all months rose by 1, 2, and 5 jiao. In the afternoon opening, it was reported that spot yarn business was quiet, but prices remained high. Japanese merchants are taking delivery this month and releasing distant months for swapping. All months rose again by 3, 4, and 5 jiao. It was found that Mai Chu sold 450 bales, Da Chang 400 bales, Shen Ji 500 bales, Yuan Da 400 bales, Heng De 400 bales, and Chang Feng 300 bales. Although spot cotton mills are not engaging in large-scale transactions, retail business is still continuous.

US Cotton Reverses Trend Before Close

Yesterday, the US cotton market opened with unfavorable news from Liverpool. Long positions were liquidated, and the Bombay gang sold off, with all months falling by 2 to 4 points. Subsequently, fellow traders bought in, and the securities and wheat markets were strong. Sellers decreased, and the market situation recovered. There were few new transactions. Fellow traders were waiting for developments from Washington. Before closing, fellow traders and foreign firms bought in, and short positions were covered. Wall Street was strong, so the closing market situation was very firm and strong. Spot cotton was up 10 points, and futures were up 5 to 9 points. (Although the budget message confirmed the possibility of expansion, the cotton market was not greatly affected. According to exchange estimates, world cotton consumption in January last year was 2,133,000 bales, compared to 2,150,000 bales in the same period last year.) The British cotton market was weak, with spot prices down 2 points and futures down 4 points. Indian cotton initially rose due to purchases by long position manipulators, but then fell back due to selling by brokers and a few retail investors. Flour Standard Often Shorted

Yesterday's flour market was steady in the morning after opening, with prices for each month being equivalent to foreign wheat. Chicago was up by between a corner and a triangle, while Canada was up by 8 fen and zero. When prices were announced, trading in each month became quiet, and the dumping of goods by various factories also became quiet. Off-market short positions were instead covered. This month, sales from the North Road to customers are active, and standard flour is often shorted, so people's confidence is tight. Distant terms are also stable because shipments are very quiet. By the afternoon opening, this month's actual sales were still active, and prices were firmly increasing. Distant terms rose step by step due to slight buying by outsiders. However, with the end of the lunar year approaching, customers are mostly closing their transactions, so future transactions will likely be temporarily quiet. As a result, this month was up 1 fen and 7 li and a half, February was up 2 fen, March was up 2 fen and 2 li and a half, April was up 2 fen, May was up 1 fen and 7 li and a half, and June was up 2 fen and 7 li and a half.

Futures Market Suddenly Rises to Cover Shorts

Yesterday, the futures wheat market turned profitable, with prices for foreign wheat continuing to be good, up by around 8 fen to a triangle and a half. When prices were announced, buying and selling this month failed to approach, and everything was sold through auctions. Distant terms rose because foreign wheat rose and spot wheat sales have stopped recently, so people's confidence is looking good. February and March were up between 3 and 4 fen. By the afternoon opening, this month opened up 4 fen due to short covering, and then prices fluctuated. Distant term transactions were still smooth, with prices similar to the morning. The situation in the spot wheat market will ultimately depend on changes in foreign wheat. As a result, this month was up 4 fen, and February was up 6 fen, March was up 4 fen. The spot wheat market has been abandoned for many days. Yesterday, due to rain, factory purchases were average. Medium-grade and lower-grade wheat prices were reduced by 2-3 fen. Shandong wheat was quoted at 4 yuan and 5 fen, Yaowan Suqian wheat was 4 yuan and another 3 fen, lower by 1 fen, and Xiangshuikou wheat was 3 yuan and 9 jiao and a half. Hua Feng, Shen Da, and Fu Feng sold over 1,200 bags.

River Rice Prices Rise Amidst Rain

(South Shanghai) The sources for each gang are similar to yesterday, with a total of over 30 establishments (nearly 6,000 shi of goods in total). Business is quiet due to rain, but people's confidence is strengthened because of the rain. Sellers are quite vocal in demanding higher prices. The supply of various superior glutinous rice from each establishment is limited. Coupled with Chiqi rice, there is more late-season rice, creating an average situation, but some have increased by several fen or jiao. Dujian rice is showing signs of strength due to shortages for two dynasties. Foreign pointed rice is still lacking, with no market and little change in price.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, over ten establishments brought goods from Hebei and the inland areas. Sales are normal across the board, and prices for white glutinous rice, guest pointed rice, and transformed yuan rice are all stable. Early thin rice is firm.

Two Ships of Guangdong Xian Rice Arrive Again

-Imported Rice Is Flat and Weak Again-

Yesterday's imported rice market situation was that because arrivals and inventory levels were full, in addition to wholesale shipments, retail arrivals were also continuous. The market fell again yesterday. New trading in imported rice yesterday was limited due to the fact that production prices were not loose. Foreign merchants were unwilling to sell low, and the whole market only opened 500 tons of Saigon rice for January delivery, thrown out by Shun Quan Long, with a price of 4 yuan and 8 jiao. Although the goods were different, this was a reduction of slightly 6 or 7 fen. There were no throwouts for March and April, so returned goods were still able to stand their ground, but trading was not much. If Ruming Foreign Firm throws out again, it may be necessary to gradually reduce prices. Spot imported rice of various Siamese Saigon rice varieties is being offered at 3,800 bags, with all prices reduced by more than slightly 5 fen. As there are relatively few arrivals and stockpiles of guest xian rice, and prices have risen at the origin, the market is more stable than imported rice. The whole city sent 4,170 bags to inland areas through this street.

A batch of Guangdong xian rice arrived in Shanghai a month ago. Because there was suspicion of being mixed with imported rice, a dispute arose. Recently, rice merchants in the South City continued to ship two batches to Shanghai, arriving by Taikoo Wheel's Zhejiang and Jiangsu ships, totaling more than 12,000 bags. High-quality goods opened at 11 yuan and 7 jiao, and low-quality goods were reduced to 10 yuan and 7 fen. All of them were directly allocated to rice shops by rice merchants and were not sold publicly at the association.

Yellow Soybeans Difficult to Stay Strong

- Several Restraints -

Yesterday's soybean market remained strong. Although trading in the market was light, sellers were determined to sell, and the market was tense. Prices continued to rise by five or six points, two jiao higher than the market last week. Currently, sources from the Jinpu Railway are unlikely to arrive due to the obstruction of war donations, and sources from the Longhai Railway are also scarce due to the joint transportation with Haizhou. Yangtze River soybeans are also scarce due to tight money and few traders, so the future of the soybean market is quite stable. Yesterday, the market opened with over 3,000 packages of Hankou Zha soybeans, which were handled by Xichang and local streets. Shashi soybeans opened with 500 packages, also destined for the interior. Factories purchased seventeen carts of Dalian Siping Street soybeans at a price of four yuan and five fen. Interior cart shops purchased three carts of large soybeans at prices of four yuan and three and a half jiao and three jiao.

Sugar Market Coarse Granulated White Rises Half a Jiao

Yesterday's currency market saw a rise in spot shortages of coarse granulated white sugar. The price of domestic green sugar rose by two or three jiao due to increased land prices, and merchants also asked for two or three jiao more, with a general trend of tightness. The Public Association quoted spot prices for ordinary coarse granulated white sugar at 18 yuan and 9 jiao, and goods from this store at 19 yuan, a rise of half a jiao. Re-exported goods were at 5 yuan and 3 jiao, a rise of seven fen. Good #9 Dutch Red sugar was at 14 yuan and 4 jiao for spot, and Taikoo B Mark was at 19 yuan and two and a half jiao. The factory's fine white sugar was also tight, with #1 being called up by one jiao to 18 yuan and 2 jiao. Guang Merchants offered 100 pieces of Shimen green at 9 yuan and 6 jiao. Dozens of baskets of Changan green were offered at 9 yuan and 8 jiao. Jian Merchants offered over 20 packages of Tongan green at 9 yuan and 7 jiao. Quanzhou red was at 14 yuan and 2 jiao. Chao Merchants' asking prices also increased as the local price of Chao green rose, requiring a premium of 10 yuan and 8, but merchants seemed to have enough goods and were watching without moving forward.

Shanghai Newspaper Local Supplement

Talks

The Completion of the North Hei Railway

- Hu Renmu

The Reuters Harbin dispatch the other day gave us a noteworthy piece of news. The news said that the North Hei Railway has been completed.

Opening a map of Northeast China, near Hailun at the northern end of the Hu-Hai Railway in Heilongjiang Province, we can find a black dot about the size of a millet grain. This is Beian Town, which is also the starting point of the North Hei Railway, and Heihe is the end point.

Why is the North Hei Railway worthy of our attention? Its own importance, it can be said, is definitely not like what the Reuters telegram said, that the wheat produced along the route will have a way to be transported and sold, and it will be a main line for developing the barren areas of northern Heilongjiang (something to that effect). Although this is reasonable and speakable, the writer believes that the place where it deserves our attention should belong to the military aspect!

We know that since Japanese imperialism forcibly occupied the four eastern provinces, it has been working hard on various constructions in the Northeast, especially military constructions. This includes the construction of railways and motor roads, the development of inland waterways, and the development of aviation networks. Railway construction is the most prominent, and the North Hei Railway is only one of them.

However, the mission undertaken by the North Hei Railway is indeed significant. Starting from the port of Najin in Korea on the west coast of the Sea of Japan (which Japan considers a key point for controlling the port of Vladivostok in the Soviet Union), the railway crosses the Tumen River and connects to the Ji-Hui Railway (Jilin to Huining). At the Lafa station, it connects to the La-Bin Railway (Lafa station to Harbin), which was completed this autumn. This is the shortest route from the Korean Peninsula to Harbin, shorter than the route from Sinuiju via Andong, turning from Anfeng Road to the South Manchurian Railway, and then to the Harbin-Changchun Line, or from Ji-Hui Road via Jilin, turning to the Jilin-Changchun Road, and then to the Harbin-Changchun Line. Harbin is an important town in northern Manchuria, and Japanese imperialism must retain it militarily whether for Manchuria or for itself (?). The La-Bin Railway crosses the river from Harbin and connects to the Hei Road. Thus, a straight-line-like reptile appeared on the map of Jilin and Heilongjiang provinces. That is to say, it is very convenient to travel from the port of Najin in Korea to Heihe in Heilongjiang, and naturally there is the same convenience in military transportation. Over the years, the Japanese imperialism has been taking a step-by-step offensive strategy against the Soviet Union. This road is the scissors for cutting off the Siberian Railway of Soviet Russia. Across the Heihe River is Hailanpao. From here, pushing forward is the Siberian Railway.

In a word, the completion of the North Hei Railway makes us worthy of attention because it more clearly exposes the further military advancement of Japan against the Soviet Union. When the future one layer by layer of advancement reaches a point where it cannot be resolved, war will naturally break out. At that time, this railway will have completed its mission.

Ten Thousand Faces

- Jing Yun

The sun had just climbed out from below the horizon, and the weather was already so hot that it was suffocating. I had to carry a bucket to the river to cool off.

According to the experience of Old "Fan Ke" (people generally and habitually regard Siam and the Southeast Asian archipelagoes as "Fan Bang" or foreign lands, and therefore those who go there are called "Fan Ke" or foreign sojourners), Uncle Changchun, as soon as the Great Heat arrives, one has to carry a bucket to the river to cool off in the early morning before the sun has climbed out. This can make the mind and body cool and refreshed, and eliminate the entanglements of disease. Although Uncle Changchun has become an old "Fan Ke" and has spent more than thirty years in "Ten Thousand Faces," he still does the same thing every time the Great Heat arrives.

("Ah, the weather is really terribly hot!")

Early in the morning, the rooster in the chicken coop under the coconut tree woke Uncle Changchun up. Habitually, he rubbed his sleepy eyes, spat out this often-recited, worn-out tune, and then, alone, carried his bucket and walked slowly to the river.

The sky was so blue that there wasn't a trace of a light, floating cloud, and it was as clear as a piece of jade covering the top of his head. Looking far away, behind the row of low houses covered with leaves of tropical plants, the tree trunks could still be clearly distinguished, and small birds flew chirping out of the nest forest. Uncle Changchun walked onto the wooden bridge, took a refreshing long breath, and immediately felt infinitely comfortable in his chest, with a natural shallow smile floating on the corner of his mouth. However, when he saw the muddy, yellow-turbid floodwaters under the bridge, and the large-scale rice shop on the other side of the wooden bridge, that huge chimney rising above the roof, lying quietly and silently like a deserted pagoda in a deep mountain, with a few small birds standing at the chimney opening, and never spitting out round and curling black smoke again, a sudden pain struck Uncle Changchun's heart, as if he had been bitten by a poisonous snake, his eyebrows tightly locked, and a dark cloud of sorrow covered his face.

("It's flood season again!") A faint breath escaped from his mouth, and his head swayed like a willow in the wind, sighing.

More than thirty years ago, Uncle Changchun thought in his heart that all of Siam, this "Fan Bang," was made of gold and that if he could go to the "Fan Bang" to be a "Fan Ke," then he could arbitrarily fulfill his desires and put gold into his pockets. Therefore, he bravely left his home, boarded a red-headed boat, drifted in the sea for more than two months, and endured all kinds of hardships before arriving in Siam. But, where in Siam was the gold that Uncle Changchun had imagined in his mind, everywhere and anywhere? When he stepped onto the shore of Siam, he finally shattered the idea of picking up gold in disappointment. However, due to Uncle Changchun's hard work and the smoothness of his business over the years, he was also able to start a family and establish a business, opening a large-scale rice shop in "Ten Thousand Faces," which made people envy him, praise him for his ability, and congratulate him on getting rich.

Uncle Changchun stood on the wooden bridge, staring at the huge chimney in a daze, thinking of the past years when the rice shop's business was booming. Whether it was day or night, this chimney, towering into the clouds, continuously spewed out wisps of curling black smoke, and the sound of the machines grinding was as musical and rhythmic as it was pleasing! Every year when the flood season arrived, after the millet spikes were cut in the mountains, they were transported along the tributaries of the Chao Phraya River in strings of boats to his rice shop in "Ten Thousand Faces." ("Seating Mountain" (in Siam, people generally call their boss "(Seating Mountain)")) thanks to your luck, the harvest this year is so good! The millet grains are so plump! Haha..." The local natives with red lips and black teeth, chewing betel leaves, said with smiling faces. Then, the workers were busy transporting the golden millet grains to the machine room to husk out the bright white rice.

But in recent years, because of the depression in the rubber industry in Singapore, workers were dismissed one after another, and the rubber factories were shut down. This caused Uncle Changchun to lose the market for selling white rice. At the same time, he could not find a way out elsewhere, and the same industry competed fiercely with each other. Under these various pressures, he declared bankruptcy.

When Uncle Changchun saw the yellow-turbid floodwaters under the bridge, and the huge chimney towering silently into the clouds, Uncle Changchun thought of the glory of a few years ago, and his ears still faintly retained the words of those red-lipped natives, saying with smiling faces... "Thanks to Seating Mountain," he felt as much pain and sadness in his heart as if he had been bitten by a poisonous snake!

Rural Farm Scenery

— Ping

The new grain has come to the threshing ground. I pushed open the window of my bedroom and looked out over the fields. Every farmyard was piled high with golden ears of grain, so heavy with yield. In the summer, it hadn't rained for more than two months. The farmers sighed and pumped water desperately, almost abandoning hope for the year's harvest. But unexpectedly, they reaped a surprising harvest. Many waxy yellow faces broke into rare smiles—smiles from the depths of their hearts.

As soon as the sun peeked over the eastern horizon, the farmers had finished their breakfast and moved the threshing bed to the farmyard to begin their work.

Curious, I slipped out the door and stood at the edge of the yard, watching.

The dew of the previous night evaporated in the sunlight, creating a misty vapor from the rice stalks, mingling with their exhaled breath in the cold wind. The old father, whose age we could no longer guess from his appearance, bravely used straw to fasten his tattered cotton-padded jacket. His two legs, like iron pillars, braced against the back of the threshing bed. He took each bundle of grain-laden rice stalks from his son's hand, raised them above his head, bent over, and forcefully threw them onto the threshing bed. After two or three throws, the grains from the rice stalks were scattered thickly on the threshing bed.

He casually tossed the remaining stalks into a corner of the yard. After the work was done, they would stack these stalks into a pile of firewood for fuel; some would also transport them by small boat to the city to sell for a meager profit, while they themselves would search for branches and fallen leaves nearby to cook their meals.

In another corner of the yard, three bamboo poles used for drying clothes were crossed, like three rifles crossed during a break in a military formation. A rice sieve was suspended from the intersection point by hemp rope. The mother held the edges of the rice sieve with both hands, her legs standing one in front of the other. The children carried the new grain from under the threshing bed to the rice sieve, and she vigorously shook the sieve. The grains fell through the sieve's holes into the prepared measuring basket below (a container for storing rice), while the rice husks remained in the sieve. In this way, they stored the new grain in their rice storage pit, to be sold off when rice prices rose in the new year.

However, due to natural disasters and man-made calamities in recent years, the farmers' rice storage pits had not seen rice husks for three years. When the new grain came to the threshing ground, it was sometimes not enough to pay the rent. Even in better years, many creditors forced them to sell the new grain at the lowest possible price—this was the manipulative tactic of rice merchants and large landlords. Rice prices were always lowest at the end of the year, and after the new year, they would raise the prices, reaping great profits from the rice they had hoarded. And those exploited farmers would then have to buy back the white rice they had toiled to produce the previous year at high prices.

Although this year had an extraordinary drought, the harvest was unexpectedly good. A scene of rural family joy unfolded on the nearby farms: the strong worked, the old basked in the sun, and even the children were constantly doing some small chores. Sparrows walked with short steps in the corner of the yard, pecking at rice grains, seeming to rejoice that they could spend a comfortable winter this year.

At noon, most of the work was completed. The farmers wiped the sweat from their foreheads with their sleeves and squatted on the yard to eat lunch. At this time, they began to notice me standing at the edge of the yard. The farmers were quite amiable. Because we often met, they especially poured me a cup of tea to greet me, so I joined their joyful group and chatted.

"The harvest is good this year!" I started the conversation.

"Thanks to the blessings of Heaven!" the old father said, his mouth full of food. "Pumping water day and night for more than two months... if the harvest had been like previous years, no one would be farming anymore..."

"In the end, it's still good for the granaries of the landlords. When the harvest is good, the rice price goes up, and we'll probably have to eat expensive rice again next year!" the mother interjected, and the old woman became worried again.

"Farmers really suffer!" the old father sighed as well. "Speaking of this year's good harvest, what about the rent we owed from previous years? We even sold an ox. If we have three more good harvests like this, I'm afraid we still won't be able to pay off a lifetime of debt!"

"What's the use of talking about our bitter fate!" the old grandmother mumbled. "Since I came over, the rice storage pit was always filled with rice. After paying the rent, we could eat and use it for a year, and still have more than two rolls (fifty yuan per roll) of silver dollars left over. Now this old bones has to suffer!"

The children held their rice bowls and chased sparrows in the corner of the yard. Did these innocent children know that they would continue their father's fate? The debt that could not be paid off in a lifetime was about to weigh on the shoulders of this generation of farmers!

On the Road to Yangjiazhai

— Youqi

The warp and weft of the roads intersect to form a complex pattern.

Indeed, that model is a net, netting the entire metropolis, netting the houses of varying heights, and also netting the different races of humanity.

Do you know? The differences are not only in the races of people. Differences in language, customs, and environment often make people different from each other, and often transform a person's temperament.

Recently, perhaps because there have been too many sad tunes, I think, whenever I walk to the end of the Jin Shenfu Road, no, or even when I just think about it, I can't help but feel a stir in my heart. Following that, I can't help but think, "This little bird, she has flown far away!"

So, my heart stirs up a more intense ruckus, doesn't it? "(A corner of the world leaves a faint mark, hearts connected in two places are truly earnest)." These parting words, you truly guessed them, they are writing the true image of my current state!

Originally, everyone was young, so there was no need to put on a face of moralism, because youth is a lovely flower, it is worthy of cherishing, of caring for. Although it grows thorns that can prick people's hands, shedding bright red blood, precisely because of this, it has even more endearing value.

Days, I don't know why they have to run so fast. It has been more than two months since she flew to the somber ancient country. Of course, that ancient country has its own special charm... golden yellow sand, low courtyard walls, neat willow banks, vast wheat fields, and scattered fruit trees... everything would make her happy. She was willing to approach them and become partners with them.

It is said that human imagination cannot always fully come true. Sometimes, it is bound to be shattered by reality. How could she have imagined it? She returned so soon, back to this bustling and detested metropolis.

In order to maintain her original opinions, she temporarily resided in the outer garden of the city.

One sunny afternoon, carrying a special mood, I left the dense net of the metropolis and stepped onto the rural road.

In the countryside, there is a different kind of sentiment. The road is a narrow strip, and the houses can be said to be genuinely domestically produced. Indeed, the scenery of the south is different. The already withered wilderness still holds a dormant life force. The early winter wind, although sharp,

Page 17

But it is very mild, and the temperature of the sun seems to be a little closer. People, also change their appearance, the simple and honest expression will make you suspect that you are in another world.

As always, she was still so happy, as if the good and evil of society had nothing to do with her.

"Do you feel good here?" She smiled, "That's right, coming here, you should also appreciate our great road." That attitude was the same as a little bird.

Slowly walking on the road of Yangjiazhai, many eyes were fixed on us.

Yangjiazhai, a small town, has two hundred households. A stone-paved road runs through the center of the entire town. The houses on both sides are so low that you can almost touch the roof with a hand. Naturally, it does not dare to be mentioned in the same breath as Europeanized grand hotels, but in its interior, it also contains thousands of things, from candies and food to teahouses and taverns. It can be said that all kinds of things are available and complete.

- Look, this is a miniature of Nanjing Road! Do you believe it? That candy store is Laoda Fang, that incense shop is the Renshen Hao of Hongmiao Fang, right? She always thinks of ways to make people laugh.

- It looks even better in the morning, with all kinds of vegetables, fish and meat, like a small vegetable market. Her mouth never stops, pointing and saying this and that.

At the eastern and western entrances, wooden barriers have been built. Needless to say, the purpose is naturally to protect the safety of the town. The fact that this form from many years ago can be found on the outskirts of the metropolis can be said to be a miracle, right?

The winter days are short. In the blink of an eye, the sun is setting again. On the way home, we are buffeted by the evening wind, watching the withered yellow fields. People who have lived in the metropolis for a long time will feel a different kind of mood.

Ms. Wang Bingmei Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Returning to Qingmen at Night - Meng Haoran

The mountain temple bells cease; it is already dusk.

The fishermen at the ferry scramble to cross.

People follow the sandy shore towards the riverside village;

I, too, board a boat to return to Lumen.

The Lumen moon illuminates the misty trees,

Suddenly arriving at Pang Gong's hermitage;

The rocky door and pine trees are long deserted and still,

Only the recluse himself comes and goes.

Farewell - Wang Wei

I dismount to offer you wine,

And ask you, where are you going?

You say, I am disheartened,

And will retire to the southern mountains.

Just go, and ask no more,

White clouds are endless.
